Deadlocked Naval Negotiations: Concerted Efforts by the United States, Britain, and Japan

Japan Presents Technical Plan to the United States

Tokyo Cabinet Decides to Unilaterally Abandon Naval Treaty

(London dispatch) The next move in the naval talks among Britain, the United States, and Japan will be a meeting between the US representative Standley and the Japanese representative Yamamoto. It is believed that Yamamoto will take this opportunity to explain the technical plan for qualitative limitations to the US representative. Yamamoto has already informed British Naval Chief of Staff Chatfield of this plan on November 30. Today, the US delegation will host a luncheon for the British and Japanese representatives. British Prime Minister MacDonald, Foreign Secretary Simon, First Lord of the Admiralty Monsell, Naval Chief of Staff Backhouse, Japanese Ambassador Matsudaira, and Japanese representatives Yamamoto and Iwashita are all on the guest list. (Reuters dispatch from the 3rd)

(London dispatch) The US delegation is adhering to its current ratio and is taking a tough stance, repeatedly threatening to end these preliminary consultations. However, after seven weeks, progress on technical details is still being made among the representatives of Britain, the United States, and Japan. The basis of discussion is still the British government's compromise proposal, especially regarding the content of the declaration of autonomy and the qualitative limitations of the forces held by each country. Specialized discussions are continuing. Apart from the declaration of autonomy, the British government does not oppose setting a maximum limit for the amount of forces held by each country. The representatives' opinions seem to be consistent on this point. As for the maximum amount of forces held, Britain and the United States advocate a total of around one million tons, which is still far from the Japanese arms reduction benchmark system that hopes to drastically reduce arms. If they confront Britain and the United States in an attempt to achieve equalization, the Japanese government will ultimately need to expand its military equipment to a considerable extent, which Japan will never agree to. Regarding other issues such as qualitative limitations, Representative Yamamoto has already met with Admiral Chatfield. The most difficult person to deal with is Admiral Standley, the head of the US delegation. The Japanese side has now decided not to talk to many people and intends to take a blitzkrieg approach. Representative Yamamoto has applied to meet with the admiral, but the US delegation stated that it can only discuss nominal equalization and absolutely opposes actual equalization, and must withdraw to its home country before the winter solstice. Given the above situation, it is still extremely difficult for the representatives of the United States and Japan to come to an agreement. If the Japanese government abolishes the Washington Naval Treaty, they will resolutely withdraw. This determination has already been expressed, and Foreign Secretary Simon has repeatedly tried to mediate, but there has been no result from his meeting with Davis. In the end, it seems that the plan to unilaterally retain the Pacific defense restriction clause has also been withdrawn. Therefore, the preliminary consultations will not end immediately and will continue for the time being with the three expert representatives focusing on numerical negotiations. (Dispatch from the 2nd by Japanese United News)

Japanese Emergency Cabinet Meeting Decides to Unilaterally Abandon Treaty

Adopting the Procedure of Consulting the Privy Council

Italy and France Are Not Deceived

(Tokyo dispatch) The issue of abandoning the Washington Naval Treaty was formally decided at an emergency cabinet meeting in the Diet at noon today, adopting the procedure of consulting the Privy Council. However, the Privy Council, considering the importance of the issue, will have a review committee examine it in detail with great care. It is expected to be passed at the Privy Council's main meeting on the 19th. Once formally decided, the government will immediately instruct Saito, the ambassador to the United States, to hand over the text of the abandonment notice to Secretary of State Hull. The date may be on the 20th. Moreover, this notice only simply states that, in accordance with Article 3 of the Washington Naval Treaty, the treaty has now expired and is therefore being abandoned. After Ambassador Saito hands over the notice to Secretary Hull, the Imperial Government will issue a simple and straightforward statement to domestic and foreign parties regarding the reasons for notifying the abandonment, clarifying the Imperial Government's policy. (Dispatch from the 3rd by Denpo News)

(Tokyo dispatch) At 12:30 PM today, the government held an emergency cabinet meeting in the Diet and decided to abandon the Washington Naval Treaty using the procedure of notification, i.e., consulting the Privy Council. The government then immediately submitted it in writing. Although the Italian ambassador to Japan did not visit the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Italian government's intention to refuse the invitation to jointly abandon the treaty is clear. Therefore, the procedure of unilateral abandonment was adopted. (Dispatch from the 3rd by Dentsu News)

(Tokyo dispatch) The Navy authorities' intention regarding the decision to abandon the Washington Naval Treaty is as follows:

The abandonment of the Washington Naval Treaty and the fair and appropriate arms reduction policy established by the Imperial Government are a natural conclusion. Therefore, once the cabinet decides, it will soon notify the countries concerned. The purpose of the abandonment is only to establish a procedure for a world peace agreement and a genuine arms reduction agreement. Therefore, even after notifying the abandonment, the government will continue friendly negotiations with the countries concerned on the arms reduction issue as before. (Dispatch from the 3rd by Dentsu News)

Japan Plans Post-Abandonment Measures after Washington Naval Treaty Abolished

Intends to Continue Negotiations with Britain and the United States

To Conclude a New Treaty to Replace the Old One

(Tokyo dispatch) The Japanese government has decided to announce the abandonment of the treaty in the middle of this month. However, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is particularly concerned that after abandoning the treaty, it will fall into international isolation. As a result of the leaders' discussions, the following post-abandonment measures have been decided: 1. The military equipment plan proposed by Japan for the preliminary talks will be promoted regardless of whether the preliminary talks break down or the treaty is abandoned, in order to implement its original intention. After the breakdown, Japan will gladly participate in the continuing committee proposed by Britain. At the same time as notifying the abandonment, it will also decide to advocate a cessation of the naval construction race and that the regular arms reduction conference next year must be held. 2. It is hoped that there will be no effective negotiations on the quantitative problem of national defense military strength. From now on, it will continue to negotiate with the contracting countries on qualitative issues from a technical perspective. 3. When negotiations on both quantitative and qualitative aspects fail, it will notify the countries that Japan is prepared to conclude bilateral or multilateral treaties with each country to prevent arms expansion or non-aggression treaties. For example, the current Four-Power Treaty still exists, and a new treaty will be concluded to expand its content. 4. All political negotiations on the Manchurian problem will be firmly rejected. However, if Japan is recognized as a stabilizing force in East Asia and its superior position is established as a prerequisite without proposing compensatory conditions, if so, Japan will strengthen the East Asian peace mechanism and can conclude new guarantee treaties with various countries. (Dispatch from the 3rd by China United News)

Britain Withdraws Compromise Proposal Due to US Opposition

Pacific Defense and Existing Ratios

US Representatives Believe They Cannot Be Separated

(London dispatch) The British government has proposed a compromise proposal, arguing that the following conditions of the Washington Naval Treaty should be retained even after it expires: 1. Various conditions regarding qualitative restrictions; 2. Article 19 regarding Pacific defense work; 3. Regulations on notification of naval construction plans. However, the US delegation opposed the British proposal because it argued that restrictions on Pacific defense work and existing ratios cannot be separated. As a result, the British government recently withdrew the compromise proposal. (Dispatch from the 2nd by Japanese United News)

Japan's Policy: Consolidating Hegemony in Asia

Japan-Russia Relations Only Superficially Amicable

Navy Seeks to Implement the Principle of Equality

丨丨Editorial in Le Temps of Paris丨丨

(Paris dispatch) Le Temps published an editorial commenting on Japan's policy, stating that Germany's diplomatic activities in the capitals of European countries are attracting much attention from Europeans. However, we must not ignore the situation developing in the Far East due to Germany's activities. Japan's aim is to overturn the traditional power of European countries in the Far East. What the Tokyo government is now committed to is not only the naval issue but also to consolidate the "Manchukuo" it created with extremely resolute actions. It is also thinking of consolidating the superior position it has gained in the areas related to the fate of Asia. Le Temps then discussed the recent declaration made by Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota to the House of Peers, saying that the general public believes that there will soon be an armed conflict. This is absolutely unbelievable. The Japanese would rather adopt a flexible diplomatic approach that adapts to the times to seek progress. The diplomatic method is certainly slower, but its results are more reliable, and Japan's diplomacy has already achieved results, which is encouraging Japan to continue. For example, relations between Japan and Russia were very tense before, but now unexpected incidents in the fishing industry no longer occur, and there is hope for a resolution of the issue of the transfer of the Chinese Eastern Railway. All of this shows the improvement in relations between the two countries. "The statement that relations between Japan and the Soviet Union are becoming good has come from the mouth of Foreign Minister Hirota. This situation is more favorable than the tense situation a few months ago, but the political problems between Japan and Russia in the Far East have not yet been resolved." Le Temps then discussed the London naval talks, saying that "What Japan seeks is not actually to fundamentally abolish various naval treaties in order to freely build a strong navy. Japan's intention is only to abolish the Washington Naval Treaty and conclude a new treaty that stipulates a common maximum tonnage so that each country can have a naval force that can truly meet its national defense needs. "A new compromise plan has been discovered in the London negotiations, indicated by Japan. The general idea is to advocate the conclusion of a ten-year agreement, in which Britain, the United States, and Japan will continue to implement their naval construction plans in the first five years. From the sixth year onwards, Britain and the United States should stop, while Japan should continue to build ships so that its naval power gradually increases until it is equal to that of Britain and the United States. (Note: The actual naval forces of Britain, the United States, and Japan have not reached the numbers set by the 5:5:3 ratio set by the Washington Naval Treaty. The so-called continuation of shipbuilding in the first five years is to make the actual naval power of the three countries reach the 5:5:3 ratio. From the sixth year onwards, Britain and the United States will maintain the numbers of 5:5 and cannot increase them, while Japan will continue to build ships in order to gradually increase from 5:5:3 to 5:5:5.) From this plan, we can also see the characteristics of Japan's policy and diplomacy, namely, it does not want to break away, but it will never give up its goals. Its method of proceeding is to strive for the point that can be reached at present. (Dispatch from the 3rd by Havas)

Opening of the French Colonial Economic Conference

Similar in Nature to the British Ottawa Conference

Aimed at Production Control and Rationalization

(Paris) Many important figures have gathered here for an economic conference. The French themselves are calling this conference the French Ottawa Conference. When the opening ceremony is held today, French President Lebrun will also attend. Representatives include governors and administrators from various French colonies, members of both houses of parliament, and prominent business leaders. Preparations for this conference have been underway for two years, but it is expected to last at least three months after its opening. The conference has several important objectives, one of which is the control and rationalization of production. Another is to investigate existing resources and future possibilities. It will also focus on the centralization of information from various regions and the harmonization of conflicting interests. This conference is said to be a cornerstone in French history. (Reuters, 2nd)

(Paris) The Economic Conference of Metropolitan France and its colonies opened today. President Lebrun, in his opening speech, stated that after a long period of preparation, it is hoped that the scattered French territories across the five continents will regain prosperity as a result. Colonial Minister Roland, in his subsequent address, explained that the goal of the conference is to "realize the economic union of metropolitan France and its colonies," and that "France has no intention of isolating itself economically from the world." He also stated that the development of economic activities in the colonies to improve the lives of the indigenous people and to ensure that foreigners purchase a considerable amount of products from French colonies is of great importance. (Havas, 3rd)

Hurricane Strikes Philippine Islands Again

Major Loss of Life and Property

Authorities Allocate Large Sums for Emergency Relief

Manila The Philippine Islands have been hit by hurricanes three times in the past seven weeks, resulting in heavy losses of life and property. The recent typhoon on Saturday and Sunday has claimed seventeen lives, with seventy people missing and 15,000 people homeless. The hurricane is now approaching northern Luzon, and it is feared that Manila will be directly affected. The Philippine Governor has approved a relief bill passed by the legislature, allocating one million Philippine pesos for relief funds in the areas affected by the typhoon seven weeks ago. At the same time, the American Red Cross has donated US$50,000 for relief efforts. (Reuters, 3rd)

Australian Storms Cause Two Kinds of Disasters

Melbourne According to news received here today, following heavy rain and gales in Victoria, floods have ensued. In the most fertile Gippsland region, seventeen people have died, and an additional six thousand people have been left homeless due to flooded or damaged houses. The local authorities are currently transporting food and daily necessities to the disaster area for relief. During the storm, the ship "Koralla" sank in the swift current, and all seventeen people on board are missing, presumed drowned. The town of Kooweerup, originally with a population of two thousand, is now completely evacuated. Six people drowned, and many others were injured by collapsing houses. Trains are now full of refugees heading to safer areas, many of whom are suffering from illness due to shock and exposure. The financial losses are incalculable. Gippsland, washed away by the floods, has become a wasteland. Railway communications in the disaster area have been disrupted, but telephone lines are still functioning. Airplanes have once again become valuable tools for disaster relief, carrying food to the disaster area and dropping it to refugees sheltering in high places. Without airplanes, these people would starve to death. More than a dozen bridges have also been washed away by the floods, making it almost impossible to reach Gippsland by boat. (Reuters, 3rd)

Asunción Paraguayan troops today continued their victorious advance, singing and dancing along the Pilcomayo River, marching straight in. England, France, and Germany Engage in New Understanding Movement

Motivation from the "German Front"

Old Warriors Abandon Grudges and Seek to Join Hands

German Special Envoy Holds Secret Talks with French Foreign Minister

(Berlin) Behind the scenes of Hitler's special envoy Ribbentrop's visits to London and Paris is a grand plan for Germany to pursue a new understanding between England, France, and Germany. The spirit of this activity comes neither from the German Foreign Ministry nor from the National Socialist Party, but from the "German Front Soldiers." This group is organized by German veterans, maintains a permanent organization in Paris, and is in contact with French veterans. Before French veterans leader M. Yvois met German leader Hitler in Berlin in November, talks were conducted by this organization. This movement began this summer, when the organization sent several copies of a speech draft of Hess, a National Socialist Party official close to Hitler, to French veterans. If the original plan had not been changed, Hess would have gone to Paris on December 15, in the capacity of a veteran, not as a diplomat. Recently, Hess and other National Socialist Party leaders have made speeches, emphatically stating that German veterans are prepared to understand their former enemies, and that there is no difficulty for former warriors to understand each other, only politicians cannot reach a compromise. (Reuters, 3rd)

(London) The British Legion headquarters here knows nothing about General Ribbentrop's discussions with British veterans. General Hamilton declared today that he had not spoken to General Ribbentrop and that he was unaware of any veterans leaders having spoken to the German special envoy. (Reuters, 3rd)

(London) In recent days, there have been rapid developments in London and other European capitals regarding the issue of disarmament. Since the British House of Commons debated imperial defense on November 29, with particular emphasis on Germany's rearmament, various countries have been initiating action. The new factor in the overall situation seems to be of a hopeful nature. The most important is the announcement by German Foreign Minister Neurath that the German government is willing to give sympathetic consideration to any proposals for a harmonious Europe. Currently, Germany is taking a "passive resistance" attitude, determined not to rejoin the League of Nations without a formal invitation, but also willing to avoid arguments that could hinder its future hopes. As for the claim that Germany may raise the issue of the return of colonies or the Polish Corridor lost after the European war, this is generally seen as premature, as this cannot be discussed until Germany's demands for equality are resolved. Although Hitler's disarmament envoy Ribbentrop's trip to Paris has aroused much speculation, it is believed that this trip will not lead to direct talks between France and Germany, as France's "let Germany return to the League of Nations first" attitude remains unchanged. At the same time, according to news from Rome, the Saar Commission is about to reach a compromise on preparations for the Saar plebiscite. (Reuters, 3rd)

(Paris) The public is very surprised by the stay in Paris of Hitler's disarmament envoy, General Ribbentrop. French Foreign Minister Laval met with Ribbentrop tonight, holding a closed-door secret talk for a long time. This meeting tonight was at the special request of the German ambassador to France. People in Paris were very surprised by this news, as it was believed that Ribbentrop had returned to Berlin. (Reuters, 2nd)

(Paris) Hitler's representative Ribbentrop is here on a private visit, hoping to take the opportunity to meet with the Foreign Minister. He asked the German Ambassador to France, Köster, to arrange the meeting. At 5 PM today, Foreign Minister Laval received Ribbentrop, and the conversation lasted for quite some time. However, Ribbentrop was only exploring opinions and was not tasked with negotiations. Ribbentrop did not seem to be carrying any specific proposals. It is generally believed that today's meeting was only a general consideration of various issues raised by the Foreign Minister in his speech to the Chamber of Deputies on Friday, which are directly related to Germany. (Laval's speech on Friday touched on inviting Germany to join the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact and the Saar issue.) What Does the So-Called "Work" Refer To?

Internal Military Forces Distrust Each Other

Religious Disputes Temporarily Eased

(Berlin) German Propaganda Minister Goebbels gave a speech to the public in Stettin, Prussia today, saying that Germany has some tasks for the future, but the time is not yet ripe. What Goebbels meant by the "future work" has aroused strong attention throughout the country. Extreme National Socialists often say that after the Saar plebiscite, foreign adventures are one of the outlets for the National Socialist Party to vent its desires, but responsible parties strongly deny this claim. There are other tensions within the country. The Stormtroopers are dissatisfied with the government, and the Blackshirts are also jealous of the superior position of the regular army, and they want to fight for the right to transfer Blackshirt officials to the regular army. However, Goebbels's views on religious issues are very different from Göring's. Goebbels's speech contained the meaning that he does not oppose the detention of opposing pastors. Major Foerster of the Wehrmacht revealed an article in the veterans' organization, criticizing the militarized Blackshirts, and his words were quite blunt, showing a glimpse of the Wehrmacht's disapproval of the universalization of the military. The element of national unity does not lie in the universal military training of the people. Non-military personnel are becoming increasingly militarized soldiers, which is causing them great anxiety. France and Germany Reach a Compromise on Saar Financial Issues

Three-Person Committee Drafts Report

Preparing to Submit to the League of Nations for Discussion

Rome Today, France and Germany signed an important agreement containing several issues related to the Saar region. It stipulates that if the Saar plebiscite on January 13 advocates that the area return to Germany, the German government will promise to pay 900 million francs as the price for the Saar mines, and pay for other items and coal 11 million tons. Last year, the Saar mines produced 10 million tons of coal, more than one million tons of iron, and about 1.5 million tons of steel. The committee ordered to negotiate the agreement will submit a report to the League of Nations on December 5. (Reuters, 3rd)

Rome The agreement between France and Germany on the Saar was officially signed at 1:15 PM. On the French side, the signatories were Ambassador to Italy Chamberlin, experts Rouef, Duback, and Misted. On the German side, the signatories were Ambassador to Italy Hassell and experts Bergel Vögdt. The agreement assumes that the Saar plebiscite decides to return to Germany, and stipulates that Germany should pay France a total of 900 million francs in debt. In addition, regarding the coal produced in the Völklingen mine in the Saar region, Germany will extract a certain amount of coal price each year and deliver it to France. The coal mine belongs to Germany, while the mine wells belong to France. The agreement does not involve political issues related to the Saar region. The three-person committee will submit recommendations to the League of Nations Council for resolution, including two layers of protection that Saar residents should enjoy after the vote, and the original rights of those participating in social insurance should be protected. The Workers' Committee has already agreed. (Havas, 3rd)

(Geneva) News that French and German experts have signed an agreement on the economic and financial issues of the Saar region in Rome has been received here with great satisfaction, believing that the task of the League of Nations Council will be reduced. The three-person committee is scheduled to complete a report tomorrow to be submitted to the Council. It is generally expected that Committee Chairman Aloisi will meet with French Foreign Minister Laval tomorrow. The extraordinary meeting of the Council is scheduled to begin at 4 PM on the 5th and will immediately discuss the report of the three-person committee. (Havas, 3rd)

Southwest Africa Merging with Germany Declaration Opposes

Mandate System Not Approved by Germany

Arbitrary Changes Not Allowed

(Berlin) The former German colony of Southwest Africa, which was entrusted to the Union of South Africa by the League of Nations after the European War, recently passed a resolution in the colonial parliament with a two-thirds majority, requesting to be merged into the Union of South Africa and become the fifth state of the Union. German newspapers were extremely angry upon hearing this news. Schnee said that Germany should resolutely oppose anyone seeking to merge Germany's former colonies in Africa and other colonies that are currently under mandate. (Havas, 2nd)

Support Eastern European Pact Plan

League of Nations Covenant Loyalty Unwavering

Estonian Capital The foreign ministers of the Baltic Entente states (i.e., Lithuania, Latvia, and Estonia) recently held their first meeting here, with the aim of consolidating peace and increasing security in the Baltic coastal area in coordination with other countries. The meeting has now ended and issued a communiqué stating, "The Baltic Entente states conference has discussed all current issues relating to general politics and Baltic coastal politics." It was decided to always adhere to the League of Nations Covenant and actively participate in the work of the League of Nations, and to express support for the Eastern Mutual Assistance Pact plan, recognizing its extreme importance. As for Baltic coastal politics, the three countries all believe that the agreement on consultation and cooperation signed in Geneva on September 12 this year has brought the relationship between the three countries closer and that efforts should now be made to consolidate it. Finally, the meeting decided that in order to adjust the foreign activities of the three countries, joint delegations will be organized in the League of Nations and various international conferences, and similar instructions will be given to ambassadors stationed abroad, so as to achieve effective cooperation. The next meeting is scheduled to be held in the Lithuanian capital between April and May 1935. (Havas, 2nd)

Romanian-Russian Diplomatic Relations Restored

Russian New Envoy Presents Credentials

Romanian Capital Diplomatic relations between the Soviet Union and Romania have been severed for sixteen years. Recently, Foreign Minister Titulescu and Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov agreed on measures to restore relations. The new Soviet Minister Ostrovsky arrived here a few days ago and presented his credentials to King Carol this morning. Ostrovsky is the first Soviet diplomat to enter the Romanian royal palace. The proceedings followed diplomatic convention. Ostrovsky, accompanied by General Irasevici, Adjutant General of the Royal Palace, entered the palace in a ceremonial carriage. A company of the Guards paid their respects to him, but because the Romanian royal family was mourning the death of the former King of Yugoslavia, no music was played. When Ostrovsky presented his credentials, Foreign Minister Titulescu introduced him. Romanian newspapers all wrote articles commenting on it. The Demingata newspaper also published an interview with Ostrovsky, outlining the Soviet Union's peace policy. (Havas, 3rd)

Kirov's Assassination Deals a Heavy Blow to Soviet Russia

The Assassin is Under Interrogation

(Moscow) The assassin of Central Executive Committee member Kirov is named Nikolaev, aged thirty, and was formerly employed by the Workers' and Peasants' Inspection Bureau. The Ministry of Internal Affairs issued a public statement saying that after interrogating the assassin all day Sunday, they learned his name, age, and previous occupation. The case is still in the preliminary stages of investigation. Kirov was a key figure in Soviet Russia, a right-hand man to Stalin. The entire country mourns his death. All streets in Moscow are flying red flags with black borders. Newspapers devoted their entire front pages to the assassination news, denouncing the "Worker's Gazette" or fascist terrorists. It is reported that Kirov was assassinated at 4:30 PM on Saturday at the Smolny Institute, the Soviet office in Leningrad. The assassin, Nikolaev, suddenly rushed into Kirov's office, took out a pistol, and shot Kirov, who was at his desk, at close range. The assassin was captured on the spot. All that is known about the assassination is this. Since Lenin was wounded in an assassination attempt in 1918, Kirov is the first Soviet leader to be assassinated. Officials say that Kirov was a revolutionary figure who was fierce, straightforward, and fearless. His assassination is the most significant blow Soviet Russia has suffered in recent years. (Reuters dispatch from the 3rd)

Leningrad Kirov's coffin is temporarily placed in the Uritzky Palace for public viewing. Representatives from various factories, collectives and state-owned farms, and institutions stand guard beside the coffin. All theaters here have suspended performances to express mourning. In the evening, residents of this city went to pay their respects. As factory whistles blew at the end of the work day, workers lined up outside the gates of each factory, waiting to proceed. Thereupon, large numbers of workers, Red Army soldiers, scientists, students, writers, artists, and government officials advanced towards the Uritzky Palace. They carried torches, portraits of Kirov, and mourning flags. The coffin was surrounded by flags and flowers. Friends of the deceased took turns standing guard. Those paying their respects shed tears. The Leningrad Academy of Sciences held a grand memorial service. Researchers and members of famous scientific societies all attended. Deputy Dean Komarov gave a speech, calling Kirov a friend of science. Researcher Yue Fei recalled the first time he met Kirov, saying that he was able to give everyone an unforgettable impression with his profound and clear thinking. The memorial service resolved to express deep mourning for this great loss, and stated that those attending this meeting will never forget the support Kirov provided for scientific work. (TASS dispatch from the 2nd)

(Moscow) Today, all newspapers published special memorial editions, containing memoirs and condolences. The Zhenwang newspaper editorial stated, "One of our country's most outstanding sons, a student of Lenin and Stalin, and a famous leader of our party, Kirov, has been murdered by an assassin sent by the enemies of the working class. The dirty hands of the enemy have cut the golden thread on the tapestry of the revolution. The enemy still wants to infiltrate the revolutionary camp to stop our progress through assassination. However, the revolution is eternal and invincible. Although the frontline commander has fallen, Commander-in-Chief Lenin remains unharmed. Although a sentinel has been assassinated, our great army fighting to build socialism remains unharmed." The Izvestia newspaper stated, "Kirov died from the enemy's bullets. Millions of laborers are outraged by the news of Kirov's death. Although the counter-revolutionary dogs who assassinated Kirov have inflicted a heavy blow on us, their expectations will not be realized. Gentlemen, you are mistaken. There have been many lackeys of capitalists in our revolutionary history, (from generals carrying bombs to feeble-minded socialist revolutionaries,) who have tried to incite Bolshevik disputes through white terror. They did not succeed even when the White Army approached Moscow and Petrograd. The Bolshevik steel front advanced resolutely, faced difficult circumstances, and ultimately was invincible. Today, our country's economy has developed greatly, and culture has also progressed. The masses have gathered around the Party. At this time, the enemy's madness and assassination can only lead to their own early destruction. Kirov was indeed the pride of our Party, and our Party's unity and its firm belief in victory have never been as strong as they are today." (TASS dispatch from the 2nd)

Leningrad Kirov's body, which was suddenly attacked yesterday, is today housed in the Poteemkin Palace. Prince Poteemkin was a famous confidant of Empress Catherine the Great in history. From dusk to midnight, workers wearing flowers and flags lined up to pay their respects to the coffin, which was illuminated by electric lights. The band played mourning music. The body will probably be moved to Moscow on Wednesday and will be kept for one day before being buried in the Kremlin Palace Garden. The police are now investigating whether the assassin had accomplices or whether it was a conspiracy by an anti-government organization. It is now known that the assassin forged documents and infiltrated the Leningrad Soviet headquarters at 4:30 PM yesterday, firing a shot that hit Kirov in the chest. Kirov died within two hours. Seeing that his goal had been achieved, the assassin shot himself in the chest with the gun, but his injuries were not serious. Kirov was 41 years old. Some believe that Kirov was Stalin's successor. (National News dispatch from the 3rd)

Importers of Foreign Wheat Request Relief from Taxation

(Nanjing) Since last year, the Ministry of Finance has levied a tax of 0.5 gold units per 100 kilograms of imported foreign wheat. Because China's flour industry relies on foreign wheat for flour production, manufacturers have been significantly affected. Recently, various factories, citing business difficulties, have specifically requested the government to provide relief and reduce the tax amount to lighten the burden. It is reported that the Executive Yuan will submit this issue for discussion at the Yuan meeting on the 4th. (Special dispatch from the 3rd)

Normal University Professor Xiao Jiewu Summoned for Questioning

(Beiping) Normal University Professor Xiao Jiewu was summoned for questioning by the Public Security Bureau yesterday. This morning, the university president Li Zheng, secretary Yi Jiewen, and dean of the College of Arts and Sciences Li Jinxi visited the Public Security Bureau. It is said that Xiao had entered the Russian Economic Institute, and there might be some suspicion. He will be released after questioning. (Special dispatch from the 3rd)

Ministry of Finance Considering Issuance of Fujian Province Public Bonds

(Nanjing) Financial circles report that the Fujian Provincial Government will issue 8 million yuan in public bonds to reorganize finances and carry out local construction. 5 million will be used to reorganize finances, and 3 million will be used for roads and water conservancy projects. A local bank will be established to regulate finance, and the province's business and slaughter taxes will be used as the bond fund. It is scheduled to be issued on New Year's Day next year, with principal and interest to be paid off in twelve years. It is heard that the Ministry of Finance still needs to consider the financial reorganization item. The construction bond for 3 million will be approved for issuance, but the nature of the business tax mentioned is unclear, and it must go through legislative procedures, so the issuance period will be delayed. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 3rd)

Central Party Headquarters Meeting Hall Completed

(Nanjing) The Central Party Headquarters meeting hall was rebuilt on the original foundation because it was not suitable for use. The capacity has been increased and the facilities are complete. It has now been completed. The meeting hall is upstairs, and the secretariat is downstairs. Arrangements are being expedited so that the Fifth Plenary Session can be held. The Secretariat's two divisions for meetings and deliberations, as well as the Secretary-General's office and the Secretariat, moved in on the 3rd. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 3rd)

Ministry of Finance Reiterates Ban to Prevent Smuggling of Silver

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance believes that although the trend of silver exports has slowed slightly, it is difficult to guarantee that there will be no smugglers. In order to strictly prevent this, it has ordered all customs tax bureaus and customs superintendents to strictly investigate. Once discovered, it will be confiscated. If smuggling exports occur, and the investigation and arrest are not effective, all tax commissioners and customs supervisors shall be punished separately. It also ordered local chambers of commerce, banking associations, and money trade associations that if silver smuggling exports occur in the future, in addition to ordering the customs to strictly investigate and arrest, once discovered, it will be confiscated and doubled penalties will be imposed. It is requested that all banks and money houses be informed to comply. (Special dispatch from the 3rd)

(Nanjing) Financial circles report that the Silver Price Stabilization Committee has now decided that the fund will be 10 million yuan, with the Central Bank and the Bank of China each contributing 4 million yuan, and the Bank of Communications contributing 2 million yuan. (Special dispatch from the 3rd)

(Nanjing) At the Ministry of Finance's memorial week meeting on the morning of the 3rd, a section chief from the Monetary Affairs Department reported on the process of levying silver export tax, roughly stating that in the 20th year of the Republic, various countries abandoned the gold standard, causing silver prices to soar, but the impact on our country was limited at this time. After the United States announced the nationalization of silver, as of October, silver outflows reached 200 million yuan. Although national wealth is based on national purchasing power, it is not surprising that some flows out, but our country is a silver standard country, and silver currency is a market bargaining chip, and it should also prevent outflows and maintain a balanced state. In order to implement fundamental measures, the Ministry of Finance levied silver export tax balancing tax, and also established a market stabilization exchange, handled exchange, and ordered customs to strictly prevent private smuggling. Since the implementation of tax collection, silver outflows have been greatly reduced, the market is stable, and people's minds are at ease. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 3rd)

Ministry of Finance Strictly Cracks Down on Unregistered Banks

(Nanjing) In light of the recent bankruptcies of various banks that have not been registered with the ministry, the Ministry of Finance specifically notified the provincial and municipal governments on the 3rd that all unregistered banks and the establishment of branches must be submitted to the ministry for registration, otherwise approval will not be granted. (Special dispatch from the 3rd)

(Nanjing) In accordance with the Savings Bank Law, the Ministry of Finance ordered various savings banks to pay one-fourth of the guarantee money. The Shanghai port has now completed this, with a total collection of approximately 60 million yuan in guarantee money. For other ports with savings bank headquarters, the Ministry of Finance has separately ordered them to promptly pay in accordance with the regulations. (Special dispatch from the 3rd)

Sichuan Tung Oil Harvest is Poor

(Nanjing) Industrial circles report that Sichuan tung oil production is approximately 30,000 tons or more per year. Last year, total exports were 1.2 million dan, with Sichuan accounting for 75%. This year, the Sichuan province suffered from banditry and drought, and tung oil production has been generally damaged, with only 50-60% of the harvest. It is estimated that tung oil production will only be 12,000-13,000 tons, and the cost will be higher than in previous years, which will not only affect foreign trade, but also severely impact Sichuan's local economy. (Special dispatch from the 3rd)

Machinery Goods Tax Will Not Be Abolished

(Nanjing) The Shanghai Machine Manufacturing Joint Association requested the abolition of the machine-made Western-style goods tax. After discussions among representatives from the Ministries of Finance and Industry and the Machine Manufacturing Joint Association, it has been decided that it will not be abolished. (Special dispatch from the 3rd)

Change of Customs Commissioner at Tianjin Customs

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance recently announced the appointment of Hirokichi Anamoto as the Customs Commissioner of Tianjin Customs, while the current incumbent, Mr. Burs, will be transferred to the post of Customs Commissioner of Hankou Customs. Anamoto previously served as the Customs Commissioner of the General Affairs Section of the Directorate General of Customs, and then requested leave to return to his country due to personal matters. He recently returned to China after taking leave and intended to return to his original position at the Directorate General of Customs. The Ministry of Finance authorities considered that the current Customs Commissioner of the General Affairs Section of the Directorate General of Customs, Ding Guitang, was effective in his work and it was inconvenient to make a sudden transfer, so Anamoto was appointed to the important post of Tianjin Customs. It is understood that Ding is the most senior Chinese official in the customs service, having served for more than 20 years and is extremely capable. When the Director General of Customs, Mr. Mallard, requested leave to return to his country, the Ministry of Finance ordered him to act as the head of the General Affairs Section. Recently, he was officially appointed. It is also heard that the government intends, in the midst of the recovery of customs autonomy, that the post of General Affairs Section will no longer be filled by foreigners. (Special dispatch from the 3rd)

Egg Yolk Lecithin Can Cure Nicotine Addiction

(Nanjing) Liu Ruiheng spoke about the method invented by Ma Wenzhao, a member of the Anti-Smoking Association, to cure opium addiction with egg yolk lecithin. Because the Golgi bodies in human cells that are destroyed by opium can gradually recover by taking egg yolk lecithin, Liu instructed Ma to conduct research at the Capital Anti-Smoking Hospital Central Hospital. It has now been completely successful. The method is simple: take 20-30 centimeters of soybean egg yolk lecithin after smoking every day. After a considerable period of time, the nicotine addiction will be cured. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 3rd)

Ministry of Communications Stipulates Procedures for Government and Military Agencies to Send Telegrams

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications decided on a method in July for government and military agencies to send telegrams, and requested the National Government to handle it. Recently, according to reports from various bureaus, if government and military agencies' printed telegram paper is handed over to committee representatives or staff to send telegrams elsewhere, the responsible official must sign or stamp the printed telegram paper in advance. There are still a few agencies that have not followed this procedure. Please give instructions. The Ministry of Communications yesterday ordered various telegraph bureaus and stations that, starting from January of the 24th year of the Republic, all printed telegram paper for official and military telegrams sent by committee representatives or staff must be signed or stamped by the responsible official in advance, otherwise they will not be sent. (Special dispatch from the 3rd)
