Battle Records of Recovering Qingliu

The bandits of Ninghua are also under encirclement.

Fuzhou Correspondence: In Fujian Province, only Qingliu and Ninghua counties in northern Fujian remain bandit areas. Wei Lihuang, Commander-in-Chief of the Eastern Route Army, after recapturing Changting, immediately ordered Lu Xingrong's troops to advance towards Mingxi and Qingliu counties. After receiving the order, Lu's troops advanced towards Qingliu in separate groups. On November 20th, they first recaptured Mingxi, engaged in searching for scattered bandits, and actively advanced towards Qingliu. On the 26th at noon, they reached the vicinity of the county town. There were about a thousand bandits entrenched in the city and the suburbs, who stubbornly resisted relying on the terrain. Several hundred more bandits also came from Xiake to attack Lu's troops from the rear. The brigade fought back in separate groups, first defeating the bandits from the outskirts and Xiake, and then besieged the city. The 311th Regiment crossed the river and charged into the city. After fighting until Shen Shi (3-5 PM), the city was recovered. It is estimated that over forty people were killed, including the pseudo-Min-Gan guerrilla commander Chen Yezhen, political commissar Lin Shengyou, chief of staff Wang Fachun, and soldiers. Fifty-odd guns were seized, over ninety bandit officers and soldiers were captured, and countless banners, publications, grain, and public cattle were seized. Over sixty male and female hostages from Yong'an and Mingxi were rescued. Over twenty bandits drowned while fleeing by jumping into the river. The remaining forces fled towards the southeast. It was found that Qingliu had been occupied by bandits for three years, the people were displaced, the fields were barren, the houses were destroyed, and the local area was extremely devastated. The streets were extremely filthy. There were less than three hundred old and young people in the entire city. Currently, Commander Lu is recruiting refugees on one hand and searching for scattered bandits on the other. Yesterday, the provincial government received another telegram from Lu Xingrong. According to reconnaissance reports, there are over a thousand bandits with eight or nine hundred guns in the Wucunquan area, seven or eight hundred bandits with four or five hundred guns in the Luofang Hekou area, and five or six hundred bandits with two or three hundred guns in the Xiake Gongfang area. Within Ninghua city, there are only over four hundred remaining bandits with over three hundred guns, but they are all starving and exhausted. As soon as the scattered bandits in the neighboring areas are cleared, they can advance towards Ninghua. The provincial government has ordered Tang Yintang, the Administrative Inspector Commissioner of the Third District, to transport salt and rice from Yanping and Yong'an to provide relief. As for the bandits in Ninghua, they are now surrounded on three sides by various units, unable to resist, and will be annihilated soon. Therefore, the complete recovery of the bandit areas in Fujian Province is just around the corner. (November 11th)

Recruitment Measures in Jiangxi Province

=Regulations on the age for military service=

=From twenty-one to forty years old=

Nanchang Correspondence: Jiangxi Province has now decided to implement conscription and has requested the provincial government through the Security Department to establish a High-Level Conscription Committee in order to implement conscription. The trial conscription measures of the Security Department are recorded as follows:

(1) All men in this province, aged from twenty-one to forty, have the obligation to perform military service and are not allowed to hire substitutes. (Period of Service) I. Active duty: six months, filled by those aged twenty-one to twenty-four. II. Reserve duty: five and a half years, filled by those who have completed active duty. III. Reserve duty: ten years, filled by those who have completed reserve duty. IV. National service: four years, filled by those who have completed reserve duty. V. Supplementary service: filled by those who are of military age but have not been drawn or selected.

Measures for deferment or exemption from military service: (1) Those who have any of the following circumstances may be granted a deferment from conscription: I. The conscription examination is not suitable for military service and is difficult to determine. II. Those who are in pre-trial public judgment detention or have been sentenced and are imprisoned. III. Due to active duty enlistment, the family cannot survive and there is solid evidence. IV. Serving in a national legal agency and certified by the agency. V. Students enrolled in school. VI. Those who have resided abroad before the age of military service. VII. If two or more people in the same family enlist at the same time, causing obstacles to family affairs, then one person should enlist and one person should be deferred. VIII. Those who cannot enlist due to illness or other unavoidable accidents should be deferred. (2) Those who have any of the following circumstances may be exempted from military service: I. Those who are disabled or deformed. II. Those who are mentally incapacitated. III. Those who have no younger male sibling. IV. If enlistment would make it impossible to maintain their livelihood and there is definite proof. V. Those who have a military science certificate from a secondary school or above can be directly assigned to the reserve service. (3) Those who are suitable men of age in each county who pass the review of the Conscription Committee will be decided by lot. (November 30th)

Northwest Inspection Notes Special Correspondent of this Newspaper, Geng Ya

The "Dry Boats" of Northwest Transportation

I woke up on the morning of the 9th feeling quite cold. Yesterday, when digging a sand well, thick ice had formed. The camel drivers removed the ice and shouted "Camel! Camel! Camel!" The camels, grazing in the distance, immediately raised their heads and came to stand beside the well (actually a long ditch), drinking with "boo boo" sounds. They drank a lot, so even if there was no water for three or four days, they could travel far without drinking. We set off at noon. The mountains were far away and the land was barren, with sparse grass. Only aged alkali flats were occasionally seen. After thirty li, we stopped at Daquan to release the camels and wait for the escort soldiers. The spring water gushed out of the cliff, flowing leisurely westward and forming a pond that could irrigate fields. There used to be over twenty families living there, but now they have all fled, leaving the cultivated land, large and small, forty-odd fields in total, and the uncultivated wilderness, as far as the eye can see, all abandoned, which is a great pity.

The next morning was the Double Tenth Festival (National Day of the Republic of China). The postman was still riding and delivering mailbags, and the camel drivers were still releasing camels and looking for firewood, as if they were unaware that today was the auspicious day of the birth of the Republic of China. Because I was waiting to meet the escort soldiers, I decided to stay here for a day. Although it was like enjoying a day of leisure on a holiday, I still felt somewhat unsatisfied because I did not get to see the national flag waving in the wind or hear the speeches of important people commemorating the festival. I happened to see a camel driver tying the camel's foot with a rope and using an awl to pierce the palm and sew a piece of leather on top. I couldn't help but be interested in studying camels again, so I continued to describe what I had not found in my previous notes about camels. The camel's palm is originally soft flesh. If it is worn out by sand and stones, it will be difficult to walk. Therefore, leather pieces are used to repair the damaged areas. When they heal, the patches fall off naturally. If traveling on coarse sand or Gobi desert, to prevent the camel's palm from being worn out, one cannot nail iron horseshoes like mules and horses, but some people also wrap their feet with leather, as if wearing shoes. If encountering a ditch that is neither narrow nor shallow, the camel finds it difficult to jump over, and it cannot step deeply into the ditch. At this time, the camel drivers even lie down in the ditch to cushion the camel's steps, which can ensure that it is not injured. When encountering a checkpoint at night and wanting to avoid taxes, one only needs to stop the bell, and the tax bureau will not hear it. This is because the camel's palm is soft and its steps are light. However, it is far inferior to the inherent ability of mules and horses to climb high and cross thresholds.

Camels are docile, strong, but timid, and are higher animals of the cold zone. They are suitable for traveling in deserts, carrying heavy loads over long distances, and can go without food or drink for four or five days. They are known as "dry boats" and "dry dragons." They are about seven or eight feet tall, and their length from head to tail is over ten feet. The humps are divided into double and single. Double-humped camels are the most numerous and are more docile, making them especially suitable for carrying goods. Single-humped camels are less numerous and are fierce and good at running, making them suitable for riding. In the deserts of southern Xinjiang and Outer Mongolia, single-humped wild camels are sometimes discovered, but they are difficult to tame and can only be hunted for food. Castrated camels are the most expensive, costing about fifty or sixty yuan each. Male and female camels are next, and only two or three male camels are left in each herd. Every time it is the mating season at the end of winter, the female camels salivate from their mouths, which is commonly called "tide." Only after the tide do the female camels lie down and mate with the male camels, which is called "laying down." After becoming pregnant, the female camels avoid the male camels as soon as they see them and do not lie down. The gestation period is after the following year, and some even gestate for fifteen months. On average, they can give birth to two offspring every three years, hence the saying "see each other twice in three years." If they give birth midway, the camel calves are loaded onto the backs of the mother camels, and the mother camels can still run together.

One year after the camel calves grow, the males are castrated, which are castrated camels. After three or four years, they can carry heavy loads. They are good for raising and can live for thirty years. However, the nose must be pierced first to facilitate pulling. The wooden stick used to pierce the nose is about four inches long and as thick as a little finger. One end is as large as an onion, or a wooden fork, and the other end is sharp. It pierces through the nasal skin from right to left. The pierced area is hollow inside, and the outside is only separated by a layer of skin and flesh, piercing through, and there are those who do not bleed. This is a natural formation. The camel rein is tied to the sharp end of the pierced wood. Pulling it hard causes it to cry out in pain. When walking, they are connected one after another, forming a line. If the rein breaks and falls to the ground, they stop. If the end of the rein is buried in a pile of soil, they dare not move. Pulling the rein and hitting the ground causes them to kneel. If two camels tie their reins to each other, they will do a "spiral dance" endlessly. The way the camel camp is arranged for the night is also based on the reins to conform. The camel I ride hates dogs walking beside it. When it sees a dog, it will kick it hard. If the dog is a little far away, before kicking it, it will lightly stomp a few steps to prevent the dog from escaping. Also, the Dunhuang Chronicle records that when a black storm is about to rise, old camels know in advance and always make a long cry. The remaining camels bury their lips in the sand. When people see their appearance, they also quickly plan to avoid the wind. Before long, the black storm arrives. Camels are huge creatures and possess intelligence, but it is unexpected that they are tied with thin reins and are forever subdued by accumulated power, daring not to easily break free, which is also pitiful.

The camel saddle is woven from wool thread, as thick as a sack, and filled with weeds to make a rectangular shape. Each camel needs two pieces, and two more pieces of wood are used to clamp the left and right sides of the camel hump. The goods are then carefully loaded on top. They can carry over three hundred pieces for long distances and four or five hundred catties for short distances. Normally, they travel seventy or eighty li per day, and ride camels can travel four or five hundred li. The annual camel transport period is about seven or eight months. During April and May, they are released into the wild and allowed to eat and rest, which is called "releasing the fields" or "striking the fields." The "releasing the fields" in the provinces of Chahar and Suiyuan often selects pastures hundreds of li away, so that they can eat and rest as much as possible and shed and replace new hair. By August and September, they are driven back for use, which is called "rising the fields." At this time, they are plump and strong, and there is no need for fodder. Until the end of the year, when the grass is withered and the meat is thin, steamed bean cakes are used, sprinkled with water and kneaded, and put in bags to hang on the camel's head. They kneel down and eat, making it convenient to load and unload. When camels lie down, they first kneel on their front legs and then bend their hind legs, and vice versa when getting up. It is commonly said that camels occupy twelve appearances: rat's teeth, cow's hooves, tiger's chest, rabbit's mouth, dragon's neck, snake's eyes, horse's ears, sheep's nose, monkey's hair, chicken's feet, dog's scrotum, pig's tail, etc. It is also said, "The head resembles a Hu sheep, the neck resembles a goose, it is neither a donkey nor a horse, nor is it a mule." Upon close observation, it is indeed correct. Camel drivers lead camels, each in order, with each person leading ten or so camels, each connected by reins, proceeding in a line. The person leading the first camel is called the "head camel," and its movements are according to their will. The last camel has a large bell hanging around its neck, ringing "ding ding dang dang," which is called the "bell ringer." If it falls off, the camel behind it stops, and the bell is silent, so people notice and return to tie it. Camels are afraid of the heat and must be released to graze, so the daily journey is mostly in the afternoon and at night. Every time they arrive at a station, they first unload the goods and then set up tents, chop firewood, cook rice, and stand watch. In Chahar and Suiyuan, they are mostly designated, while in Gansu and Xinjiang, they are mostly rotated. Each driver receives a monthly salary of about six yuan in Chahar and Suiyuan, and only two yuan in Gansu and Xinjiang. The food is rough, the work is heavy, and the treatment is harsh, which urgently needs to be improved.

In various parts of northwestern China, transportation is mostly underdeveloped, and in the vast wilderness deserts, it still relies on camel transport. According to reports from Nanjing, the total number of camels in the country is 2,637 in Outer Mongolia, 80,000 in the four provinces of Ningxia, Suiyuan, Chahar, and Rehe, 58,000 in Heilongjiang, 50,000 in Xinjiang, 50,000 in Qinghai, and 20,000 in Shaanxi and Gansu, totaling 260,637. It can be said that camels still occupy an important position in the transportation of the Northwest.

Appeal from the Silk Weaving Industry in Shandong Province

=Silk prices have fallen and many silk businesses have been suspended=

=One-third of the mulberry trees in Linqu have been uprooted=

Jinan Correspondence: The silk industry has always been prosperous in the Linqu Zhoucun area of Shandong Province. Linqu County alone used to sell more than 4 million yuan worth of silk in the 17th year of the Republic (1928). The silk weaving industry in Zhoucun was also developed in the past. All its products, silk fabrics, were known as Dong goods, also known as Zhoucun goods. Although they are not as beautiful as those produced in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, they are more durable, which greatly benefits rural areas and promotes industry and commerce. In recent years, due to the sharp drop in silk prices, the impact has been significant. The Zhoucun Silk Weaving Industry Association, Dyeing Industry Association, and Silk Merchants, considering their livelihoods, jointly sent a letter to the Shandong Min Guomin Daily, requesting the Construction Department to promote domestic silk in order to prevent foreign goods, save the industry, and relieve rural areas. The original letter is as follows: "We believe that the land of Qi and Lu has long been known as a region of mulberry and hemp, with the silk industry accounting for half of it. Since the founding of the Republic, the government has repeatedly promoted it, and mulberry trees have covered almost all the fields of eastern Shandong. In recent years, raw silk has been in a slump, and many merchants have gone bankrupt. A visitor from Linqu said that one-third of the mulberry trees in his county have been uprooted to bake tobacco leaves, claiming that if the cocoon price remains the same, they will be completely removed. The efforts of promoting mulberry planting for years would be in vain, which is a great pity. According to the investigation, one-third of the silk businesses in Zhoucun have been suspended, and nearly 10,000 workers have lost their jobs. The remaining capable ones have also switched to weaving foreign hemp. Tens of thousands of workers are working hard day and night to promote foreign hemp, which is hateful. At present, the price of silk has fallen by eight-tenths compared to the past, which is unprecedentedly low. A foot of plain twill iron machine silk, weighing one tael, costs no more than two jiao. Silk gauze costs one tael and one jiao, including the labor cost. The price is the same as cloth, but it is twice as strong and durable. If the directors of the various departments can uphold the spirit of helping the people and purchase some pieces, sell them in various counties, and persuade people to love the country, so that civil servants, gentry, merchants, and scholars who wear Zhongshan uniforms can use domestic goods, and since the material is good and the price is the same as cloth, everyone will surely be happy to follow. The virtue of a gentleman is like the wind, and the superiors act as an example, and the inferiors will certainly follow. If the industry can thrive as a result, and the flood of foreign hemp can be stopped, there will be good results, and the people will benefit greatly, not just the farmers, workers, and merchants," etc.

Guangzhou Kidnapping and Murder Case

The Kidnapped Victim Was a Section Member of the督配局 (Supervision and Allocation Bureau)

Lured and Imprisoned in a House Under the Pretense of Selling It

The Kidnapped Victim Was Killed and Two Kidnappers Were Arrested

Guangzhou Correspondence: Recently, a major kidnapping case occurred in this city, causing a sensation in society. The victim's family kept it a secret at the beginning of the case. It was not until the end of March, when the case was solved and the victim was murdered, that the outside world learned the truth. The details are recorded as follows:

Disappearance: Zhong Dejie, a native of Fangcheng County, residing on the third floor of No. 12 Huiji West Road, Guangzhou City, was a section member of the Guangdong Provincial River督配稽查 General Bureau. Because he was the younger brother of Bureau Chief Zheng of the督配稽查 Bureau and his family was wealthy and extravagant, he attracted the attention of bandits. A month ago, Zhong had told his friends that he planned to spend a large sum of money to buy a building, and several friends had introduced him to houses for sale. On the 2nd of this month, Zhong returned home after finishing his work, and a friend invited him out to inspect a house for sale. Unexpectedly, he disappeared without a trace, like a yellow crane. His family posted notices to find him, but there was no news for several days.

Ransom: A few days later, the Zhong residence suddenly received a letter from the bandits, stating that Zhong Dejie was being held captive and demanding that they quickly raise 100,000 yuan and hand it over to a designated location to secure his release, otherwise his life would be in danger. The letter was signed with a certain bandit gang's name. Only then did the Zhong family realize that Zhong had been kidnapped by bandits. They immediately sent someone to negotiate the ransom with the bandits and reported the matter to the authorities, requesting them to arrest the bandits. Zhong's relatives were all powerful and influential, so detectives were dispatched everywhere, and the investigation was extremely strict. The bandits, knowing that the situation was urgent, sent a second letter, urging the victim's family to quickly prepare the ransom. The Zhong family did not respond. The bandits then put Zhong to death. At the beginning of this month, a third letter came, asking the Zhong family to send someone to the Changdi Zhongshan Hotel to negotiate.

Arrest: Police detectives and representatives of the Zhong family went to the Zhongshan Noodle Shop as agreed. At 7:00 PM on the 23rd, the representative suddenly received a phone call, ordering them to bring the ransom to redeem the victim the next day, otherwise the kidnapped person would have no hope of survival. At this time, the caller's voice was identified by the police detectives. They immediately tracked the phone call to its origin, and found that it came from a Western restaurant on Changdi. The detectives immediately went there and found that the caller was still sitting there, dining with a female companion. The detectives stepped forward and asked for his name. The guest scolded them, saying that they were being abrupt. The detectives recognized that his voice was the same as the bandit who had called the Zhongshan Hotel. They immediately tied him up. The guest initially tried to quibble, but was later taken to the Public Security Bureau's Detective Section for investigation. After much questioning, the bandit confessed the mastermind of the case. The main culprit was then arrested immediately.

Confession: According to the main culprit's confession, he and six others lured Zhong Dejie on the 2nd. First, a close friend of Zhong falsely claimed that there was a mansion at No. 14 Ren'an Street, Xiaobeimen, and urged him to go and see it. When Zhong arrived, they immediately detained him, intending to demand a ransom of 100,000 yuan. Later, Zhong's family deliberately delayed, and reported the matter to the authorities for investigation. The accomplices, seeing police everywhere, feared that once the matter was revealed, they would not be spared. If they released Zhong without conditions, it would be even more difficult to gain a foothold afterward. Therefore, on the night of the 6th of this month, they strangled Zhong to death with a rope and buried his body in the basement of the house, in order to cover up their tracks.

Discovery of the Body: After hearing the confession, the police detectives immediately dispatched officers to escort the criminals to No. 14 Ren'an Street, Xiaobeimen, as guides. When they arrived, they found that the people in the house had already moved out, and a "For Sale" sign was posted on the door. Inside the door were two or three construction workers, repairing the walls. The police detectives pushed open the door and ordered the criminals to point out where the body was hidden. The workers dug in the basement of the left room of the house. At a depth of about two feet, a foul smell filled the air. Another foot deeper, Zhong's body was completely exposed, but most of it had already decomposed. Later, the court's coroner also arrived at the scene to examine the body and found three rope marks on the deceased's neck. The deceased's clothes still had the督配局 badge. It was confirmed that he had been strangled to death. After completing the coroner's report, the deceased's family took the body back for burial the next day. The truth of the case was thus revealed. However, the authorities said that of the six criminals, only two have been arrested. The other four are still at large. They are now intensifying their efforts to track down the escaped bandits so that they can be tried together with those in custody. (November 28th)

Jiang Song: Hunan Refugees Causing Disturbances in the Countryside

The county government recently received an urgent telegram from Shihudang Township, reporting that nearly one hundred people claiming to be refugees from Hunan were gathering crowds and causing disturbances in the Zhangzhuang area, taking the opportunity to loot and pillage, and could not be stopped. They requested that a team be dispatched to suppress them. After receiving the report, County Magistrate Jin immediately dispatched the Security Brigade's Water Patrol Team to the countryside to suppress the disturbances and reassure the local residents.

Provincial Government Committee Member Visits Songjiang for Inspection

Ye Xiufeng, a member of the Provincial Government and Standing Committee member of the Provincial Anti-Smoking Committee, came to Songjiang today by private car to inspect the county government and the Anti-Smoking Committee. It is said that he instructed the director of the committee to strictly investigate and punish those who smoke without a license and those who set up private smoking dens. Once a case is discovered, they should be severely punished according to the law. He returned to Shanghai that evening.

Kunshan: Bandits Loot Two Villages

Last night, a large number of bandits, forty or fifty in number, suddenly arrived at the second village of Manzihang Ge Cemetery in the Sixth District. They spoke in mixed accents and were all armed with guns. After arriving, they looted all the residents of the two villages. They did not leave with their loot until dawn today, heading towards Dianshan Lake. It is said that the two villages suffered heavy losses. The district chief, Dai, is now going to investigate in order to report to the county government for strict investigation and arrest.

Editor of New Kunshan Daily Detained

Wu Xingbo, the director of the Kunshan County Public Security Bureau, sent detectives to the New Kunshan Daily yesterday afternoon to arrest the editor, Feng Yi, and put him in custody. For a time, there was much discussion in society. After inquiring in many ways, reporters learned that the reason for the detention was leaking military secrets (the county security team was stationed in various townships). Another said that on the evening of the 27th of last month, when sixteen policemen from the Public Security Bureau went to Lu Wenhuan's house in Chejiabang, outside the Daxi Gate, to arrest gamblers, they were resisted. A policeman, Liu Tianwu, fell into the river and drowned. The next day, Feng wrote an article about it, implying that the police were arresting gamblers and even suffered drowning. Another said that Feng had recently tried to extort money from a butcher shop without success, which led to the accusation. It is not known which is true, so it is recorded here to await verification.

Wuxi: Rice and Paddy Rice Are Crowded and Sales Are Stagnant

The sales of rice in this county's market have recently tended to be stagnant. On the supply side, a large amount of foreign rice from Shanghai has arrived. There are about six or seven hundred boats of indica rice and paddy rice from southern Anhui coming to Wuxi. However, domestic sales are quite sluggish, so prices, even if they do not fall sharply, will inevitably have a slight decline. It is difficult to predict the rise and fall of market prices next year. According to yesterday's market opening, new white japonica rice was 12 yuan to 11.4 yuan, white yuan rice was 13.3 yuan, Jiangbei white yuan rice was 11.45 yuan, white passenger indica rice was 10 yuan to 11 yuan, Du Yuan wheat was 5.7-8 yuan, Du yellow beans were 6.5-6 yuan, and Saigon rice was 11.1-2 yuan.

Baojia Bridge Robbery Case: Victim Wounded by Knife

Hua Renfa, a resident of Baojia Bridge near Dongting in the second district of the county, is a farmer by trade and has a small amount of land, which led to him being coveted by bandits. At about 10:00 PM the night before last, thirteen or fourteen bandits suddenly came, speaking in a strong northern accent and carrying刺刀 (bayonets) and watermelon knives. They opened the back door and entered the house, pulling Hua's wife, Tang, out of her warm bed. They forced her to reveal where the silver was hidden, injuring her arms and flanks. They also stole clothes, jewelry, silver dollars, and other items. At the time, the victim, Hua Renfa, was in the middle of making rice and rushed out of the house to a neighbor's house, ringing the gong to raise the alarm. The bandits then left with their loot, leaving behind a兇刀 (murder weapon). The incident has been reported by the camp to the County Public Security Bureau, which has ordered strict investigation and arrest.

Jiangyin: Director Yin Inspects the Zhencheng Road

The paving of the Zhencheng Road is gradually being completed. The sections between Wuben and Longhutang and Zhenjiang have been opened to traffic one after another. Shen Qi, the director of the Provincial Highway Administration Office, set off from Tianzhen on the 2nd in a single-seater car to inspect the road surface along the way. He arrived in Cheng at 2:00 PM and returned to Zhenjiang in the same car. The full road opening ceremony will be held on New Year's Day next year. According to Director Shen, the road surface construction along the way is good. The operation of long-distance buses is currently being tendered for.

Nantong: Coastal Areas Defend Against Bandit Raids

The nine coastal areas of Nantong have suffered from repeated raids by sea bandits. Although the bandit ships have been repelled by the teams, it is difficult for the police teams to stay for a long time. Currently, the local militia are following the defense measures set by the Nantong District Security Headquarters, building bunkers at key locations at the sea entrance, and having the fishing teams guard them day and night to prevent bandit ships from invading.

Haimen: County and City Bus Station Fire

Xu Shaolong's house at the county and city bus station caught fire at about 1:00 PM yesterday (the 1st) due to carelessness while cooking lunch. Suddenly, thick smoke billowed and flames soared, alarming the entire city. The fire brigade and the Public Security Bureau chief and police rushed to the rescue. It took more than an hour to gradually extinguish the fire. It is estimated that six houses and miscellaneous items were burned down, worth more than 2,000 yuan.

Verdict on Corpse Money Sharing Case

In March of this year, a floating corpse was found at Yujiaogang in the first district, with more than 1,000 yuan in banknotes in its clothes. It was found by villagers Wang Shihua and Zhu Xianglang, who intended to embezzle it. Later, it was learned by local gangsters Xuan Changhai and Yang Sili, who detained Wang and Zhu in a room, threatened them in every way, and ordered them to hand over the original money and share it. Later, the township chief Liu Hui reported the matter to the county government, which ordered the police to arrest Wang and Zhu. Shi and Yang were on the run. During the interrogation, Wang and Zhu both confessed. The sentence was announced the other day: Wang Shihua and Zhu Xianglang were sentenced to two months in prison. Shi Changhai and Yang Sili were on the run and have not been caught. They are being wanted.

Jiaxing: Fengqiao Maoshengfeng Pawnshop Suspends Business

Since the three money shops and one bank in Jiaxing declared liquidation, the Zhongjie Da錩pawnshop, Wangdian Renxin pawnshop, and Puyuan Gongyi pawnshop have all been affected and have declared suspension of pawn and waiting for purchase. As a result, poor farmers have no way to pawn their goods. Currently, the local people have submitted a petition to the Construction Department, requesting that it order the pawnshops to resume business so that the poor can have access to funds. Unexpectedly, the Maoshengfeng pawnshop in Fengqiao Township, a county affiliate, also used the excuse of being affected by rural bankruptcy and having accumulated goods, and announced the suspension of pawn and waiting for purchase yesterday. The farmers there will again experience the pain of not being able to pawn their goods.

Opening of County Councilor Election Ballots

The Jiaxing County Councilor election was held on the 2nd at the township offices. At 5:00 PM, the ballot boxes were sent to the district offices, and the ballots were opened in the district offices starting on the 3rd. However, in this election, those who hoped to be elected made efforts in many ways, and the material losses were countless. There were also several ballot boxes that were not sealed by the supervisors, so there were many rumors among social figures. It is also known that citizens such as Shen have telegraphed the provincial government to control the dispersal and to re-elect the government.

Huzhou: Bandit Li Xiangfang Executed by Shooting

Li Xiangfang (also known as Li Changshou), a bandit who had repeatedly committed kidnapping and robbery, was arrested by Huang Yuqing, the captain of the Criminal Investigation Team of the Wuxing County Public Security Bureau, in a grass shed in Donglin Mountain in July. After County Magistrate Dai interrogated him, Li confessed to the kidnapping and robbery without hesitation and was sentenced to death. The sentence was submitted to the province for approval. The approval was received from the province the other day. At 10:00 AM yesterday, the county government sent more than ten members of the cadre team to the Public Security Bureau's Relic Institute to bring out the bandit Li Xiangfang. After the county secretary, Liu Yuwu, questioned him about his age and origin and verified his identity, he was escorted to the South School Yard for execution by shooting.

Hangzhou: Wandering Youth Commits Suicide Due to Poverty

Zhang Yulin, a resident of Yanguan Lane, Fengshanmen, Hangzhou, was 28 years old and had a small amount of property. After his father passed away, he was allowed to wander around. He did not listen to the advice of relatives and friends. All his property has now been completely exhausted. Now that it is the cold winter, he is facing economic difficulties and has no cotton clothes to wear. He had the idea of suicide. The night before last, he hanged himself in a mulberry garden at the foot of Ziyang Mountain. His sister heard about it. In addition to applying to the court for exemption from inspection, she bought a coffin for burial herself.

Xiaoshan: The Suffering of the People in the Southeast and East Due to Disasters

The autumn harvest of crops in the four townships of Xiaoshan was poor. The farmers' economy has reached its limit. Recently, the weather has turned cold suddenly. In the Shahe East Township and the sixth and seventh districts of the East Township, the general disaster victims are calling for cold and hunger, and the situation is very tragic. There are even daily reports of people selling their sons and daughters. There are also dozens of disaster victims from outside the city and local poor people begging along the streets.

Local News

British Minister to China, Sir Miles Lampson, Arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong Yesterday Morning

Then Visited Mayor Wu at the Municipal Government

Wu Ding Set Up a Banquet at Noon to Welcome Lampson

British Minister to China, Sir Miles Lampson, accompanied by the Counsellor of the Embassy, Eddington, and Secretary, Borough, left Pingnan at the beginning of last month to inspect the British businesses in various ports of South China. Now that he has completed his official duties, he and his entourage have taken the British steamship company's Goff and set off for Shanghai from Hong Kong. He arrived at the port at about 9:00 AM yesterday, berthing at the Gonghexiang Wharf in Hongkou. Those who went to the pier to welcome him included Yu Ming, the director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, British Consul-General in Shanghai, Bailey Nan, President of the British Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai, Marshall, and more than 20 British citizens residing in Shanghai. The Public Concession Police Department also sent several Chinese and Western detectives to the pier to be on alert. After Lampson briefly exchanged greetings with the welcoming members on the ship, he disembarked and took a car directly to the Hwa Wai Hotel to rest. It is said that he had a very good impression of his tour of various places in South China. If he has the opportunity in the future, he still intends to travel to other parts of China. Regarding the issue of the elevation of the rank of the envoys of China and the United Kingdom, the authorities of the two countries have not yet raised it for discussion. He plans to stay in Shanghai for several days and then return to Beijing via Beijing, he said. Lampson then went to the city center at 11:30 to visit Mayor Wu. Wu personally received him. He left after about 20 minutes. It is said that this visit by Lampson to Wu was the first official visit after the presentation of his credentials. Wu Shifeng, in addition to returning the visit this afternoon, also decided to host a banquet at his private residence on Haig Road at 7:00 PM that evening. It is also known that Lampson has agreed to the invitation of the United Pacific Society and is scheduled to attend the society's lecture on international issues at the Licha Hotel at 12:30 on the morning of the 6th. Wang Zhengting, the former Minister of Foreign Affairs of our country, will serve as the chairman of the association at that time.

Shanghai South Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Will Hold an Air Defense Drill This Morning

A Preliminary Rehearsal Was Held from 3:00 AM to Dawn

A Formal Event Will Be Held at 3:00 AM Tomorrow Morning

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration is holding air defense exercises along the line, and the stations have held them one after another. Shanghai South Station is scheduled to implement it tomorrow morning. A preliminary rehearsal was held this morning, from 3:00 AM to dawn. The details are recorded as follows:

Preliminary Rehearsal This Morning: Shanghai South Station held a preliminary air defense rehearsal this morning. Zhong Wenjiang, the head of the Shanghai-Jiading section of the Transportation Department, served as the general commander. Han Shangying, the head of the Shanghai-Jiading section of the Police Department, served as the deputy commander and managed the police sentries. Zhou Binwu, the station master of Shanghai South Station, was responsible for transportation management. Engineer Luo Shengyuan was responsible for disaster relief management. Liang Peigen, the head of the Shanghai-Jiading section of the Locomotive Department, was responsible for lighting management. Ma Shaoping, the director of the Police Department of the Two Railway Bureaus, guided everything. The rehearsal methods were decided at a joint meeting yesterday afternoon.

Issuing General Mobilization Order: At 3:00 AM this morning, a report came from the Longhua Road telephone that five or six enemy planes had taken off from Jiaxing and were attacking Shanghai South Station. After receiving the call, the South Station master, Zhong Wenjiang, issued an order to prepare for defense, and all the lights along the line and inside the station were turned off. All the staff of the Railway Bureau immediately set out in accordance with their assigned duties, and a general mobilization for prevention was launched. All the railway police immediately patrolled the road, announcing a special curfew. Anyone passing by must be inspected.

Enemy Air Raid: The South Station telegraph operator immediately sent a telegram to each station to report the enemy planes' movements and the places they passed. When the enemy planes arrived, they used lime bags as bombs to bomb the bridges, tracks, and stations along the way. The houses along the line had caught fire. The station immediately dispatched people to put out the fire, rescue the injured, and send craftsmen to rush to repair the bridges and tracks. At the same time, the families of railway personnel and residents along the line were taken in, and the station's freight yard was designated as a shelter. After the enemy planes left, traffic and lights were restored.

Formal Exercise: After the preliminary rehearsal this morning, it was decided that the formal exercise would be held at 3:00 AM tomorrow morning. The Two Railway Bureaus specially sent senior personnel such as the director of the Secretariat and section chiefs to serve as judges. Those who made efforts in air defense will be rewarded. After the major stations on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway have completely held the exercises, the grades will be assessed and rewarded separately based on the results of each station.

Ministry of Finance Instructs Municipal Chamber of Commerce and Other Groups to Prevent Smuggling of Silver Goods

They Must Provide Sincere Assistance

Notify All Merchants to Comply

The Ministry of Finance instructed the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Silver and Money Trade Association yesterday, saying: "The purpose of the Ministry's collection of silver export tax and balance tax is to preserve wealth and stabilize the market. The impact of this concerns the well-being of the whole country. However, recently, some unscrupulous merchants have only sought private gain and disregarded the overall situation, and have often smuggled silver goods for export. This illegal profiteering is extremely hateful. The Ministry has already strictly ordered the customs to carefully investigate and arrest these merchants. However, the aforementioned smuggling is complex and varied, and the official's eyes and ears may not be comprehensive. In particular, all legal organizations should turn to joint supervision. If smuggling of silver goods for export or instigation of smuggling is discovered, it should be reported to the nearby customs office immediately. In areas without customs offices, the local government should be secretly reported to detain the goods first, and then submit them to the Ministry for verification. All the goods will be confiscated, and the amount of smuggled silver will be doubled as a penalty. If a merchant reports the situation and leads to the seizure, 40% of the fine will be used as a bonus to encourage them. The name of the original informant will be kept confidential by the ministry. All legal organizations have close financial relations and must provide sincere assistance in order to achieve the effect of mutual support. In addition to issuing separate orders, all merchants are hereby ordered to comply with the above, and so on."

Shanghai Does Not Allow Conscription

Transportation Office Soldiers and Soldiers Are Punished

Central News Agency reports that on November 9th, Zhang Mingyue from Shaoxing came to Shanghai from his hometown to look for work. He was passing by the outer Ma Road of the 16th Pier and was lured by Zhou Jinbiao, a transporter from the Zhedong Office of the Fourth Recruitment Office stationed in Shanghai, to the Nanhuiguan and forced to join the army. After his brother, Zhang Zhongjian, learned about it, he reported it to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters and requested rescue. The headquarters sent personnel to investigate and found that Zhang Mingyue had been assigned to the Engineering Company of the 36th Division by the Transit Office. The headquarters ordered the New Soldier Transit Office to quickly bring Zhang Mingyue back to the headquarters for verification. Afterwards, Zhang Mingyue was released from the Engineering Company and reported the details of the abduction to the headquarters. As Shanghai does not allow conscription, it has already been ordered to be implemented. A letter was also sent to the Zhedong Office of the Fourth Recruitment Office to investigate. It has now been heard that the transporter Zhou Jinbiao has been dismissed and punished. Li Ren, the adjutant of the Transit Office, was given a demerit for not paying attention to the counting of new soldiers. An strict order was given to all transportation personnel not to have this type of situation occur again when sending soldiers to Shanghai.

Mr. Yu Jichuan Discusses Hunan Province Issuing 10 Million Yuan in Public Bonds

=Two-Thirds for Road Construction, Remainder for Old Debts=

=Approved by the Executive Yuan, Issuance Imminent=

=Initial Loan of 250,000 to Complete the Hunan-Guangxi Trunk Line=

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, Yu Jichuan, a member of the Hunan Provincial Government and concurrently Director of the Department of Construction, arrived in Shanghai by plane from Hunan on the 29th of last month to discuss mortgaging 10 million yuan of Hunan Provincial Construction Bonds to obtain a loan. He is staying at the China Hotel. A reporter from Xin Xin News Agency paid him a special visit yesterday. According to Mr. Yu, the 10 million yuan in public bonds has been approved by the Executive Yuan and is generally not a problem. To complete the Shanghai-Guangxi highway trunk line within a limited time, an initial loan of 250,000 yuan will be borrowed from banks such as the Bank of China for use. Everything has been negotiated, with Hunan's salt tax and highway revenue as collateral, at a monthly interest rate of 1%, to be repaid in five months. The mortgage matter for the public bonds has also been discussed with various banks and finalized. After the bond certificates are printed, he will come to Shanghai again to continue the process. The details are recorded as follows:

Guarantee Fund for Issuing Public Bonds According to Director Yu, in order to complete the three highway trunk lines of Hunan-Guizhou, Hunan-Sichuan, and Hunan-Guangxi, the Hunan Provincial Government specially decided in a meeting to request the Central Government to issue 10 million yuan in public bonds to meet urgent needs. The issuance methods and guarantee fund for the public bonds have been submitted to the Central Government by the Provincial Government and have been approved by the Executive Yuan. Once approved by the Central Political Council, the bonds can be issued, and there is generally no problem. The guarantee fund will consist of Hunan's deed tax and the provincial business tax as the primary guarantees, and all highway revenue as the secondary guarantee. In the future, representatives will be sent by the Ministry of Finance, the Audit Department, the Hunan Provincial Government, the National Economic Council, and the banking community to form a Hunan Provincial Construction Bond Fund Custody Committee to ensure seriousness.

Determined Use and Mortgage Negotiation The use of the public bonds has been decided: one-third, or more than 3 million yuan, will be used to settle Hunan's old debts; two-thirds, or more than 6 million yuan, will be used to complete the three highways: Hunan-Guizhou, Hunan-Sichuan, and Hunan-Guangxi. During this trip to Shanghai, he has repeatedly contacted Zhang Gongquan, General Manager of the Bank of China, Tang Shoumin, General Manager of the Bank of Communications, and Chen Guangfu, General Manager of the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank. With the assistance of the banking community, they have all expressed their approval of the mortgage principles. The Hunan Provincial Government plans to first solicit bids for printing the bond certificates, and then, depending on the need, mortgage the designated 6 million yuan in bond certificates to the banking community in installments. Therefore, the current contact with the banking community is only to exchange opinions and agree on principles. Once the public bonds are reviewed and approved by the Central Political Council and printing bids are solicited, he will come to Shanghai again to continue discussions.

Hunan-Guangxi Highway Loan Negotiated The Hunan Provincial Government has already started construction on the three highways of Hunan-Guizhou, Hunan-Sichuan, and Hunan-Guangxi according to plan. Commander-in-Chief Chiang of the Military Affairs Commission recently ordered the completion of the Hunan-Guangxi Highway for traffic within one month to facilitate transportation from Hunan to Guangxi and ordered the National Economic Council to allocate funds for subsidies. Although 50,000 yuan has been received for use, it is still far from enough. Therefore, during this trip to Shanghai, he contacted Zhang Gongquan, Tang Shoumin, and Chen Guangfu of the banking community to borrow 250,000 yuan. All negotiations have been completed. The loan will be provided by the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, with a monthly interest rate of 1% and a term of five months, with Hunan's salt tax and road revenue as collateral. The contract has been drafted and will be brought back by Mr. Yu to report to the Provincial Government for approval. After approval, it will be formally signed in Changsha with the lending banks.

Hunan Province Builds Three Major Trunk Lines The Hunan Provincial Government is currently actively building three major highway trunk lines: (1) the Beijing-Guizhou trunk line, from Taohuaping in Hunan to Huang County on the border of Guizhou, approximately 400 li long, has already started construction and a portion has been opened to traffic; (2) the Beijing-Sichuan trunk line, from Taoyuan in Hunan to Youyang in Sichuan, approximately 400 li long, has already started construction and will be built in stages; (3) the Shanghai-Guangxi trunk line, from Hongqiao in Hunan to Huangsha River in Guangxi, approximately 300 li long, has already started construction and is scheduled to be completed for traffic within one month. After the completion of the above three trunk lines, transportation between the capital and the provinces of Hunan, Guizhou, and Guangxi will become more convenient.

Returning to Nanjing and then Hunan to Report Director Yu told the Xin Xin News Agency reporter at the end that after arriving in Shanghai, he once went to Nanjing to meet Commander-in-Chief Chiang to report on the highway construction situation and met with Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi to explain the guarantee fund and allocation of the 10 million yuan construction bonds. With the matters in Shanghai completed, he decided to take the 11:00 PM express train to Nanjing tonight (i.e., last night) to apply to the National Economic Council for subsidies for the Hunan-Guangxi highway project. He does not plan to stay in Nanjing for long and will return to Hunan to report.

Ministry of Railways Plans to Utilize Remaining Boxer Indemnity Funds

To Build One New River Steamer and Two Motorboats

The Ministry of Railways' loan from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity totals 400,000 pounds. It was originally planned that 260,000 pounds would be used to build ocean liners and 140,000 pounds to build Yangtze River steamers. However, the cost of building the ocean liners reached over 346,000 pounds, leaving a balance of only about 50,000 pounds. The Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board has repeatedly sent letters to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company inquiring about this matter to resolve it as soon as possible.

Building a River Steamer The remaining Boxer Indemnity funds, calculated at the current gold price, amount to no more than 700,000 yuan, which is only enough to build one Yangtze River steamer domestically. If built in England according to the contract, it would not be enough to build even one vessel. The board of directors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has repeatedly discussed this matter and decided that no matter what, the remaining Boxer Indemnity funds will be used to build one river steamer first and will not be diverted to other uses. It has repeatedly consulted with the Boxer Indemnity Committee and has been approved to build the steamer in Shanghai.

Two Motorboats In the end, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Boxer Indemnity Committee have agreed that one Yangtze River steamer, generally similar to the Taikoo Dockyard's Wusong steamer, will be built in China. In addition, two 500-ton motorboats will be built for use on the upper Yangtze River. The shortfall will be funded by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and a report has been submitted to the Ministry of Railways for record. The designs of all the new river steamers are in the planning stage at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and construction will begin as soon as they are finalized.

Page 9

Sinking of the Taishan, Bound for England, Confirmed

Bodies Retrieved 140 Miles Off Qingdao

Total Loss of Ship and Cargo Estimated at Over 300,000 Yuan

All 45 Crew Members Presumed Dead; Compensation to Be Provided

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, after the Taishan, belonging to the Sanbei Shipping Company, disappeared en route from Qingdao to Shanghai, the British warship HMS Peterel recovered the bodies of four crew members of the ill-fated Taishan 140 nautical miles off Qingdao. The search continues in the coastal area. The company has decided to provide compensation according to the law. Details are as follows:

After Disappearance The Taishan left Qingdao at 2:00 PM on the 26th of last month, carrying 3,000 tons of coal bound for Shanghai. After encountering a strong wind and disappearing, the coastal radio station repeatedly called the Taishan, but received no response. It then telegraphed all coastal ships for help, but received no response. The (XNDF) signal received by the Changxing in Shanghai a few days ago was actually a radio signal from other ships calling the Taishan.

Confirmed by British Warship HMS Peterel, which was anchored in Weihaiwei, recovered four bodies wearing life preservers 140 nautical miles off Qingdao while sailing to Shanghai. The life preservers were marked with the name "Taishan." The warship telegraphed the British Consulate in Shanghai, which notified the Sanbei Shipping Company yesterday. The bodies have been transferred to the British warship.

Retrieving Bodies After receiving the report from the British Consulate, the Sanbei Shipping Company requested the British warship to continue searching for bodies. The British warship has dispatched small boats to search the coastal shallow water beaches and the location of the Taishan's accident, as well as other items on board, to confirm the incident.

All Crew Presumed Dead The captain of the Taishan, a Norwegian named Hai Lie, the comprador Lu Jingtang, the second mate Huang Yuanquan, the chief engineer Zheng Yongqing, the first assistant engineer Lou Longhua, the second assistant engineer Sun Wanqing, one foreman of the sailors, six sailors, one foreman of the stokers, nine stokers, two oilers, two carpenters, four helmsmen, one radio operator, and the chief steward, cook, and Western servants, totaling 45 people, are all presumed dead. The radio operator Yu Shoude had taken sick leave and was replaced by an agent sent by the company, and thus escaped the disaster.

Total Loss According to Yu Shunfu, assistant manager of the Sanbei Company, whom the Xin Sheng News Agency reporter met yesterday, the hull of the Taishan was in good condition. The company's insurance department had self-insured it for 100,000 yuan. The ship is currently valued at approximately 200,000 yuan, and the 3,000 tons of coal it was carrying are worth over 30,000 yuan. If it is confirmed that it has sunk, the total loss, including the crew, will be approximately 300,000 yuan. As for the crew members who died, compensation will be provided according to the law after confirmation.

Family Members of Crew Members All crew members of the Taishan, except the captain, were Chinese. Since the ship disappeared, family members and relatives of the crew members have gone to the Sanbei Company on Guangdong Road every day to inquire. After hearing that the British warship had recovered the bodies of the Taishan 140 nautical miles off Qingdao, they were extremely alarmed. Although they did not cry out loud, many shed tears. However, the company is still comforting them, as the bodies recovered by the British warship have not yet been identified.

Director of the Ping Sui Railway Bureau, Shen Chang, Arrives in Shanghai to Discuss the Recent Situation of Rectifying the Ping Sui Railway

Revenue Increased by Half, Debt Restructuring Successful

Thoroughly Revamping Railway Administration, Emphasizing Technical Talents

Since the Ping Sui Railway was taken over and directly managed by the Ministry of Railways last summer, personnel have been sent to rectify it, and significant progress has been made. Shen Chang, Director of the Railway Bureau, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing yesterday to meet with Gu Mengyu, Minister of Railways, to report on the railway administration. A Daily News reporter interviewed Mr. Shen at his hotel and inquired about the recent situation of the Ping Sui Railway. He provided a detailed account, which is recorded below:

Revenue Increased Sharply Mr. Shen first answered the reporter's question about the revenue situation of the Ping Sui Railway. In the past seven years, the revenue was only over 7 million yuan. After rectification, the revenue increased sharply. The revenue for last month (November) reached 1.1 million yuan, and the revenue for 1934 is approximately 10.5 million yuan, an increase of half compared to before. As for expenditures, they have also been greatly reduced, saving 1 million yuan per year. The current expenditure is only 6 million yuan per year.

Restructuring Debt The railway's internal and external debts amount to 90 million yuan, of which Japanese debt accounts for approximately one-third. It has been impossible to restructure the debt in the past. Recently, through my efforts, I have been working on restructuring the debt. The Japanese debt has now been completely restructured, and one-third of the American debt has also been restructured. Debts to domestic banking groups, small material merchants, employee savings, and arrears have been restructured to 90%. As a result, the total amount of debt has been reduced to 60 million yuan, and interest has been suspended and the principal is being repaid. This year, 2 million yuan in cash has been paid out.

Improving Railway Administration Mr. Shen continued, "I am determined to thoroughly improve railway administration. The sleepers of the railway have not been replaced for ten years, and most of them are rotten. Since the Ministry of Railways took over, 500,000 sleepers have been replaced, costing 1 million yuan. 150 freight cars have been added, worth 900,000 yuan. In addition, approximately 1 million yuan has been added for machinery and parts. The stations west of Suiyuan have been completed for ten years, but have not been built. Now, the two major stations in Baotou and Salachi have been completed, and the remaining eight stations will be completed next year. The passenger cars have also been greatly renovated. There is a special express train once a day, with electric lights and heating equipment. Construction has also begun on three new trains, which will be completed next spring. The cost is only 25,000 yuan per car, which is almost half the price of imported cars."

Emphasizing Technology As for the sole guiding principle for rectifying the railway, it lies in emphasizing technical talents. Minister Gu believes that the Ping Sui Railway is notoriously difficult to manage, so technical personnel from various locations are selected based on their abilities. For example, Jin Shixuan, Director of the Transportation Department, is a leading expert in transportation studies in China. Pan Shanwen, Director of the Accounting Department, has been the manager of the Zhongfu Bank for more than ten years and has a long-standing reputation. The Directors of the Engineering and Mechanical Departments both have over 20 years of experience in their respective fields. As for lower-level staff, such as station masters and clerks, promotions and demotions are based on examination methods. I will stay in Shanghai for a few days and then return to Beijing to resume my duties."

Chinese National Products Participate in the Philippine Carnival

Preparatory Meeting Held Yesterday

Chinese national products will participate in the Philippine Carnival, which will open next year. The first preparatory meeting was held at the Yiyou Society Clubhouse on Hankou Road at 3:00 PM yesterday. Guo Shun, Hu Xiyuan, Ye Hancheng, Wang Hanqiang, Fang Yexian, Chen Yiting, Wang Jian, Qian Chengxu, and Lu Xingzhuang attended. Hu Xiyuan chaired the meeting, and Qian Chengxu recorded the minutes.

Determining the Name The draft charter was passed: (1) Name: Preparatory Committee for Chinese National Products Participating in the Philippine Carnival; (2) Address: 115 Hankou Road; (3) Funding: To be determined after the conveners consult with the municipal government. The amount will be discussed and estimated by the conveners and other preparatory committee members first; (4) Organization: Mayor Wu Tiecheng was elected as the chairman of the preparatory committee. It will be divided into six groups: General Affairs, Finance, Design, Transportation, Solicitation, and Review. The Review Group will be composed of experts hired by the preparatory committee. 1. General Affairs Department: Guo Shun, Hu Xiyuan, Qian Chengxu; 2. Finance Department: Guo Shun, Fang Yexian; 3. Design Department: Ye Hancheng, Wu Zhihao, Chen Yiting; 4. Transportation Department: Lu Xingzhuang, Chen Yiting, Wu Zhihao; 5. Solicitation Department: Wang Jian, Wang Hanqiang, Chen Binghui, Qian Chengxu; 6. Review: To be appointed separately. The funding budget will be submitted to the municipal government for instructions. The amount of funds will be drafted by the design organization and submitted to the municipal government for review.

Telegram from Luzon The Philippine authorities sent a telegram to Mayor Wu: (1) The first letter and telegram inquired whether Chinese merchants participating in the carnival to display goods could be exempted from customs duties. The telegram has requested General Manager Leg to find a way. If possible, taxes will only be levied on the sale of goods and inquire about the cost of establishing a Chinese goods display. The carnival has directly telegraphed the reply to you; (2) Exhibition samples, if the value is within 10,000 Resos (approximately 20,000 yuan) and it is declared that they will be shipped back within six months without being exported, can be exempted from taxes with a guarantee. As for the cost of temporary storage space, it depends on the quantity of goods and the area occupied, but the amount must be limited.

Scheduled Opening According to a China Eastern News Agency reporter, the carnival is scheduled to open on February 1st next year in Little Luzon. The annual meeting is scheduled for February, so the preparatory committee is actively working. The preparation period is tentatively set at six weeks. Well-known domestic products from all over the country have been formally solicited. Letters have been sent to solicit participation from all over the country.

Philippines Welcomes According to Hu Xiyuan, a member of the preparatory committee, the Philippine people are very welcoming to Chinese national products. In the past, when the island held exhibitions, Chinese manufacturers who participated all achieved excellent results. This is an excellent opportunity to promote Chinese goods in the Philippines. The preparatory committee has decided to ship the exhibits to the Philippines on January 14th. If delayed any longer, it may be too late.

Yarn Factory Association Held a Meeting Yesterday

To Discuss Ways to Rescue Chinese Yarn

According to the Da Gong News Agency, recently, Japanese yarn sales have suddenly increased, and the export volume has seen a sharp increase. The sales of Chinese yarn are becoming more sluggish. The National Federation of Chinese Yarn Factories held its 13th joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees at its headquarters on Avenue Edward at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss ways to rescue the declining yarn industry. Details are as follows:

Meeting Situation The executive and supervisory committee members who attended the meeting yesterday included Rong Zongjing, Guo Shun, Nie Lusheng, Wang Qiyu, Huang Shoumin, Xue Chunsheng, Su Taiyu, Dong Zhongsheng, Yang Hanxi, Liu Mengjing, and others. Guo Shun chaired the meeting. It started at 2:00 PM. In addition to discussing the production, sales, and transportation of cotton yarn, the rest were general affairs matters. According to the committee members present, the discussions yesterday were limited to internal issues, and there was no need to publish the proposals. The issue of imposing unified taxes was also not discussed.

Rong Zongjing's Remarks According to Rong Zongjing, a giant in the yarn industry who has just returned from the Northwest after investigating the production and sales of cotton, "I went to Henan, Shaanxi, and other provinces this time to inspect the agricultural production situation. I feel that there has been a significant improvement in wheat and cotton. Domestic yarn factories and flour mills will be able to stop relying on foreign wheat and cotton in the shortest possible time, saving the country 40 to 50 million yuan per year. The cotton seeds in Anyang and other counties in Henan and Shaanxi were improved varieties that I bought and distributed in Shanghai in previous years, and the quality is better than before. In my opinion, the cotton produced in Hebei is the best, but the production volume is very small and does not meet the needs of Shanghai yarn factories. I hope that people in the yarn industry will do their best to promote the cultivation of improved varieties and resist foreign cotton."

Since the cultural relics from the Beiping Palace Museum stored in Shanghai were reorganized into three groups to work simultaneously, the work rate has increased. Ouyang Daoda, director of the museum's Shanghai office, and Shu Chushi, a member of the supervisory committee, have agreed to add another group from yesterday to make it four groups working simultaneously. It is estimated that 15 boxes of porcelain and two boxes of jade were sorted yesterday morning and afternoon.

Hu Society Plans to Hold a National Silk and Satin Exhibition

In view of the increasing encroachment of foreign goods on domestic silk and satin in recent years, the Hu Society has separately submitted reports to the National Government, the Military Affairs Commission, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Interior, ordering all subordinate units to wear blue robes and black jackets made of domestic silk at all gatherings, commemorative weeks, and weddings, funerals, and banquets to highlight the national style and revitalize silk and satin. The instructions have been approved and forwarded to the subordinate units for compliance. The society is planning to hold a joint National Silk and Satin Movement with the Shanghai Silk and Satin Trade Association to promote this. A Chinese Silk and Satin Exhibition will be held at the society for three days starting on New Year's Day in 1935 to display various valuable domestic silk fabrics for exhibition and promotion. Ministry of Railways and Municipal Government Plan to Build a Railway in the City Center

Funds Allocated by the Ministry, Roadbed Provided by the Municipal Government

Construction to Begin Next Spring, Section to Be Completed Before the National Games

The Ministry of Railways is cooperating with the Shanghai Municipal Government to build a railway in the city center to help develop the city center. Construction will begin after the completion of the Shanghai-Xiangshui double-track railway. Details are as follows:

Construction to Begin Next Year The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus have been ordered by the Ministry to build a railway in the city center. The detailed plan has been drafted and approved by the Ministry. It has been decided that construction will begin in January next year after the completion of the double-track railway between Shanghai and Xiangshui at the end of the year. The funds will be allocated by the Ministry of Railways, but the roadbed will be provided by the Shanghai Municipal Government. The route will run from Songhu Road along Sanmin Road to connect with the Songhu Railway. It is expected to be completed and open to traffic before the opening of the National Games.

Building a Section First The original plan for the city center railway was to start from the Songhu Railway, run along Sanmin Road to Songhu Road, and reach the Qiujiang Wharf, with the aim of prospering the city center and realizing the Greater Shanghai Plan. As the National Games will be held in Shanghai next year, to facilitate transportation, it has been decided to build a section of track to the city center first. The section to Qiujiang Wharf will be carried out at the same time as the construction of the wharf.

Ministry of Railways and China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to Implement Lianyungang-Qingdao Joint Transportation Tomorrow

Yongji Steamer Sailed to Hai Yesterday, First Voyage at That Time

Joint Transportation on Other Routes Is Being Prepared

Since the completion of Datonggang, the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Lianyungang Railway Bureau have been planning joint transportation from Lianyungang to Qingdao, Tianjin, and other places. Joint transportation to Qingdao has been prepared and is scheduled to be implemented tomorrow. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company dispatched the Yongji steamer from Shanghai to Lianyungang at 2:00 PM yesterday. It is scheduled to load joint transportation goods from Lianyungang on the 5th and make its first voyage to Qingdao. The Tonghua steamer has also been dispatched from Shanghai to Lianyungang to load joint transportation goods and sail to Qingdao. The Haixiang and Hairui steamers have also been designated to sail depending on the joint transportation goods.

Joint Transportation Prices Goods from various stations along the Lianyungang Railway, such as Daguang, Lingbao, Shaanxi, Luoyang, Zheng County, Lanfeng, Shangqiu, Tongshan, and Xin'an, can be handled by joint transportation. The price from Lianyungang to Qingdao is 28 cents per ton, plus the railway freight from a certain station along the line to Lianyungang. The ships sailing on the Lianyungang-Qingdao route will sail from Shanghai to Lianyungang, load Lianyungang Railway joint transportation goods and sail to Qingdao, and then load Jiaoji Railway joint transportation goods and sail to Shanghai.

Other Routes Joint transportation from Lianyungang to Xiamen, Shantou, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou is being prepared and will be implemented after the implementation of joint transportation to Qingdao. Before implementation, goods from Lianyungang to Xiamen, Shantou, Hong Kong, Guangzhou, and other places must be transferred through Shanghai. Joint transportation from Lianyungang to Tianjin was originally planned to be implemented soon, but it has been temporarily suspended due to the problem of freight caused by the impending freezing of Tianjin. It will be implemented after the thaw next spring.

Robbery in Broad Daylight on Guling Road, Two Robbers Captured Alive

Older Sister Holds Young Child to Watch the Robbery

Child Injured by a Stray Bullet

Yesterday at approximately 1:30 PM, a certain Mr. Jia was walking near the intersection of Guling Road and Park Road when he was suddenly confronted by five bandits. Two of them were armed with handguns. They emerged from the side of the road, blocked his path, and ordered him to remain silent. Meanwhile, the unarmed bandits searched his person, and as a result, more than seventy yuan in paper money was robbed and scattered as the bandits fled. Upon seeing this, Mr. Jia frantically shouted for help, crying "Catch the robbers!" The bandits, in desperation, fired a shot backward. However, the nearby police officers had already been alerted and, upon hearing the gunshot, immediately drew their guns, gave chase, and returned fire. At the same time, neighboring police officers also came to encircle and apprehend the robbers. Although the bandits fought as they ran, they were gradually overwhelmed and scattered in flight. However, two of the bandits ran out of bullets and were cut off. They were captured alive by the police officers, and a handgun was seized. They were immediately taken to the police station for detention. However, when the police officers were returning fire at the bandits, a young child named Huang Erniang, aged two, who lived at No. 36 Shunxing Lane, Taiping Lane, Park Road, was being held by an older sister playing at the entrance. Hearing the commotion of catching robbers, the older sister, not realizing the danger, actually went to watch while holding Huang Erniang. As a result, Huang Erniang was injured by a stray bullet. Afterwards, a police vehicle sent her to Bao Long Hospital for treatment. Whether her life is in danger is difficult to say.

French Concession Police Department Breaks Up a Major Fraud Case

Gambling Establishments are Never Allowed in the French Concession

According to news from the French Concession Police Department yesterday, recently there have been rumors that Mr. Meriel, the French Consul-General in Shanghai, has taken leave to return to his country, and that these people have obtained permission from the new French Consul who is acting for Mr. Meriel, to open gambling establishments in the French Concession. After a secret investigation by the French Concession Police Department, it was found that a certain Mr. Pan had arranged to meet on November 30th at a hotel on Dongxinqiao Street. The police department sent a detective, posing as a representative of a capitalist, to negotiate. Mr. Pan said that he could obtain a document from Wu Zhang, but it would require 225,000 yuan, and there must be deposits in the bank. Mr. Pan arranged for the detective to have a second meeting at a restaurant on North Sichuan Road that evening, and a third meeting was arranged for December 1st. On that day, during the negotiations, there was another detective posing as a capitalist. At that time, there were eight swindlers who finalized the previous terms and confirmed that 1 million yuan would be deposited in the bank. A contract was signed on the spot and handed over to the capitalist (i.e., the detective posing as such). The swindlers agreed that a certain Mr. Zhou, who had not yet arrived, would lobby the French Consulate. At that time, five detectives who were stationed in the adjacent room rushed into the room and arrested the swindlers on the spot and brought them to the police station. They admitted the above facts and confessed to seeking capitalists to open gambling establishments in the French Concession. Important documents related to the flower association organization were found on the swindlers. Under interrogation by the French police, one of the defendants confessed that the French Consul-General was about to take leave to return to his country, and the new Consul had been instructed by the French government to allow the opening of five gambling establishments. However, the owners of the gambling establishments would have to pay 45,000 yuan per month to cover various expenses. The French police are now stating that the rumor is completely untrue, and that gambling establishments are never allowed in the French Concession, regardless of the nationality of the people. The Police Department hopes that residents will report any information about similar fraud schemes at any time.

Stray Bullet Injures Maid, Miss Shen Er

Madam Xie Xu, a woman from Zhenjiang in her late thirties, residing at No. 2, Jinyu Lane, Avenue Montegnie, French Concession, was suddenly visited by five robbers armed with handguns at 6:10 PM last night.
