Although the story is concentrated on drama, the beginning of that bizarre story to the end of the ending, the cause of a storm, is entirely because of raising funds for the nursery, launching a recreation party, and causing a family comedy between a certain wife.

Promoting the holding of nurseries, especially being able to use it in movies, the harvested effect is expected to be great. I hope everyone will pay great attention to it. At the same time, I hope the producers can be more cautious in their attitude. (Gratitude)

Local Customs Anecdotes

Examination of Kang Senghui's Dwelling in Longhua

— Shanghai Communication Agency

The pagoda in front of today's Longhua Temple in Shanghai is said to have been built in the tenth year of Wu Yiwu. However, it is said that this is the case, but there is no definite evidence. Now there is a Dragon Flower Relic Record stele under the pagoda, which briefly says:

At that time, I heard that Kang Senghui was of high moral character and passed through Longhua Tang. The dragon gave way to his residence and built a thatched hut for self-cultivation. King (Sun Quan) recognized the monk and met him, and persuaded him to worship Buddhism. ······The King ordered the construction of thirteen pagodas, Longhua being one of them.

Although it clearly states that Kang Senghui once lived in Longhua, this pagoda was built to commemorate the place where he lived; however, this statement is also unknown and cannot be believed.

Now, reading Kang Senghui's biography from the Buddhist scriptures, it briefly says:

Kang Senghui, his ancestor was from Kangju. He lived in Tianzhu for generations. His father moved to Jiaozhi because of business. When he was over ten years old, his parents both died, and he became a monk. At that time, Sun Quan had already controlled Jiangzuo, but Buddhism had not yet been practiced. So he traveled east with his staff and reached Jianye in the tenth year of Chiwu, where he built a thatched hut and set up images to practice Taoism. Quan summoned and said to him: "If you can obtain relics, I will build a pagoda for you." He fasted and respectfully requested, and indeed obtained relics. Quan was greatly surprised and convinced, and built a pagoda for him immediately. Because there was a Buddhist temple for the first time, it was named Jianchu Temple. Its place was named Buddhato-ri. He translated many scriptures at Jianchu Temple. He died in April of the first year of Taikang of Jin.

According to the biography, he came to Jianye (now Nanjing) from Jiaozhi (now northern Annam), and there is no doubt that he came east by sea. Then, he may have landed at a seaport near Shanghai today and built a thatched hut in Longhua. The biography says, "He reached Jianye in the tenth year of Chiwu and built a thatched hut and set up images to practice Taoism." At first glance, it seems that he built a thatched hut in Jianye. In fact, reaching Jianye is one thing, and building a thatched hut and setting up images to practice Taoism is another thing. The biography does not clearly state where the thatched hut was built. Because Shanghai was remote at that time and had no place name, it was not mentioned in detail. However, since today's Shanghai is within the scope of the so-called Jiangzuo, how can we know that the thatched hut was not built in Shanghai!

The names Jianchu Temple, Buddhato-ri, etc. cannot be verified in later generations. Let's leave it blank for now. However, since he came to Jianye from Jiaozhi by sea, it seems possible to say that he landed at a seaport near Shanghai today; it was reasonable to build a pagoda at that time as a memorial.

I secretly think that the pagoda built at the beginning must have been extremely simple, so it was not seen in the records and poems of previous people. As far as my knowledge is concerned, the earliest poem about Longhua is Rimei's poem about passing through Longhua at the end of the Tang Dynasty. The poem says:

The ancient temple still exists in the city today, and people walk on the frosty grass bridge. I still hate the dim moon for its dim light, and I can't see the reflection of the pagoda in the heart of the wave.

Carefully examining the meaning of the first sentence, the temple had already been destroyed at this time (note, the temple and the pagoda were not built at the same time), so it is said that "the name of the ancient temple still exists." As for the sentence "I can't see the reflection of the pagoda in the heart of the wave," it seems to refer to the absence of the moon, and has nothing to do with the existence or abolition of the pagoda, but the meaning is also very vague.

Now, checking the old records about the rise and fall of the pagoda, many details are also unknown before the Song Dynasty. After the reconstruction in the second year of Taiping Xingguo in the Song Dynasty, there were clear records. As for the pagoda seen today, it has been rebuilt many times. However, based on the path of Kang Senghui's eastward journey, it can be said that the trace of his footsteps once reached a sea, and the beginning of the pagoda's creation was built to commemorate the place where he lived, which can also be a saying.

Securities

Securities Where Ups and Downs Are Not Easy

Yesterday's Market First Rose, Then Declined Slightly

Cotton Yarn Delivered That Is Higher Than the Stored Sample Is Also Allowed to Be Delivered

The city's yarn and cloth exchange market announced that the standard products or substitutes provided for delivery by cotton yarn trading brokers should be consistent with the stored samples of the exchange before they can be allowed to be delivered. Now, it is reported that various substitutes listed in the exchange's cotton yarn grade table, when sold in the market, have different packaging than before. For example, there are those who have changed the smooth 16-count yarn to 16.5-count, and there are also those who have changed it to 17-count, and are marked on the package. When this substitute is provided for delivery, if the goods are confirmed by the exchange to be consistent with the stored samples, only the packaging is slightly different, and the difference is indeed higher than the stored samples, it can also be allowed to be delivered, and the receiving broker shall not object. It has been decided by the board of directors in accordance with the provisions of Article 169 of the business rules.

U.S. Cotton Private Estimates Slightly Increased

New York Telegram, 1st. The Khu-Khwaik Company's estimate for the current new cotton crop is 9,696,000 bales, with 9,112,000 bales already ginned. The previous estimate (October 31st) was 9,617,000 bales.

Grain Futures Rise Initially, Then Decline

Yesterday's flour market started steady and then declined. The price of foreign wheat, Chicago, rose about 45 cents, Canada rose 234 cents or so. After the opening, the price of foreign wheat, coupled with the lingering effect of the previous week, made the openers feel quite strong. The price for this month opened at 5.10 cents, but although the opening price was good, it gradually weakened. Because the situation of Tianjin spot flour was not good, the Tianjin dealers were eager to sell. The opening price for January and beyond was initially stable, but then customers began to sell off, and some factories also hedged. Therefore, after the second session, the price fell steadily, making it difficult to recover, falling by 12 cents or so compared with the initial opening. By the afternoon session, the market atmosphere gradually deteriorated. Recently, due to the sluggish demand from Tianjin dealers, and rumors that a factory had ordered a ship of foreign wheat at 68 cents, the selling pressure for all months increased slightly, and the market atmosphere felt weak. As a result, this month fell by 2.5 cents, January fell by 2.75 cents, February fell by 2.25 cents, March fell by 2.75 cents, April fell by 3 cents, and May fell by 2.5 cents.

Wheat Futures Decline Significantly

In the wheat futures market, when the opening price was set, the market participants were generally watching, and the trend was flat. Later, as the flour market strengthened and then weakened, although trading was not very active, the market atmosphere loosened by 23 cents or so. By the time of the afternoon opening, trading was still quiet. However, the flour market reversed and fell due to actual sales returns, and rumors continued to circulate about another ship of foreign wheat being ordered. Therefore, the long-term sentiment gradually weakened, and the fluctuations compared with the closing price of the previous week were quite significant. January and February fell by 8 cents, and March fell by 10 cents. The spot wheat market is still stable. The opening price for Xuzhou Shandong white wheat is 3.94 yuan, the second grade is 9.20 yuan, and Yaowan wheat is 3.90 yuan, the second grade is 8.90 yuan. Fuxin sold 6,000 bags, Zaofeng sold 3,000 bags, and Shenci sold 1,000 bags, it is said.

The main reason for the stable market on the 1st was the lack of sellers of Chicago wheat and the firm market conditions in Liverpool. It is rumored that several places are using wheat instead of corn for feeding livestock. A well-known Chicago trader is currently recommending buying May oats.

Glut of Japonica Rice, Sluggish Sales

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, over forty dealers from various regions arrived, bringing over six thousand shih of goods. Sentiment remained weak, and the market atmosphere was soft. Local sales were normal, and dealers from other regions sold off their bagged rice due to the daily price declines. It is estimated that Qingdao, Yantai, Weihaiwei, and Tongzhou dealers bought a total of 1,400 to 1,500 bags. The selection was strict, and the bids were tight, so it did not help the overall situation. As a result, the price of late indica rice continued to fall by about 10 cents, and the price of thick japonica rice also fell by over 10 cents. Duyang Tip rice followed the trend of foreign rice, falling by about 10 cents. Only the price of Yin Bian Yuan rice remained largely unchanged.

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, twenty-six or twenty-seven dealers arrived from the river regions, with over two hundred and ten boats in the river. In terms of market sales, the demand for loose white japonica rice was normal. The demand for bagged rice for restaurants improved slightly. Sales of Yang Du Tip rice declined compared to the previous improvement. The sales of new and old white Yuan and Yin Yuan loose rice were still good. Liquor stores continued to buy. Early thin indica rice was still good. The consignment of Tip rice from outports was sluggish. The early market for white japonica rice was flat and weak. At noon, a small amount of high-quality rice rose by a few cents, while medium and lower quality rice rose by a few cents to nearly 10 cents. The prices of Yang Tip and Du Tip rice rose slightly by a few cents. The prices of early thin indica rice, new and old white Yuan and Yin Yuan, and Tip rice from outports remained stable.

First Batch of Tianjin Rice Arrives in Shanghai

丨Foreign Indica and Local Indica Sales Both Strong丨

Yesterday, sales of both foreign and local indica rice were active, but production prices were high, and the intentions of hoarders were very firm. Moreover, the local demand was also active. Yesterday, the market price rose by 5 cents. Holders of futures rice did not sell, which people also took as a sign of hope. Later, Da___ released 1,750 bags, and Yali Jinlong, two foreign firms, released 1,250 bags, totaling 3,000 tons. The price also seemed firm. April Yuan grain reached as high as 5.05 yuan, long grain was 5.02 yuan, and December was 4.92 yuan. All were bought by local dealers. Currently, there are 5,500 bags of foreign rice open for sale. It was previously reported that the first two small shipments of Tianjin rice arrived in Shanghai yesterday, totaling 343 bags. Because the owner's asking price was too high, no sales were made. The quality is better than Annam japonica, but not as good as Changbang machine-milled japonica. Yesterday, local indica rice was snatched up by Changshu and Zhejiang dealers, and the market changed from weak to brisk, with over 10,000 bags offered, mainly Shashi brown rice, totaling over 7,000 bags.

Sesame Sales from Foreign Firms Still Good Despite Price Drop

丨Estimated at Over 40,000 Tons丨

Since the activity of sesame sales from foreign firms began, statistics show that since the new crop came on the market, there have been transactions of over 40,000 tons. The price has risen from 7.70-7.80 yuan to 9.50 yuan. Yesterday, the market softened slightly, with 100 tons traded at 9.30 yuan. The price fell by 20 cents, so sentiment in the market was unstable. Fortunately, the sales to other regions were still relatively good, preventing an excessive decline. Yesterday, 40 bags of Gaoyou sesame, 230 bags of Mingguang sesame, 51 bags of Taizhou sesame, 150 bags of Zhangbaling sesame, and 250 bags of Yingzhou yellow sesame were offered. Please refer to the market price column for price drops in the local Zhejiang and Shaoxing regions. Initially, soybean prices fell sharply by 10 cents due to the sudden drop in standard bean prices, causing sentiment to weaken, and prices fell by 7-8 cents. Later, news came that Dalian had rebounded, and the market atmosphere stabilized. Currently, there are inquiries from Tongzhou, local dealers, and inland factories, so the market situation is not too dire.

Japonica Rice Market: Local Factory White Rice Exceptionally Firm and Expensive

Yesterday, the sugar market was generally flat due to the firm customs gold unit, but actual sales remained sluggish. The association's list price for number 24 coarse granulated white sugar was 18.55 yuan, delivery at the pier was 18.65 yuan, transit goods were 5.20 yuan, number 89 Dutch red high-quality sugar was 14.10 yuan, with some transactions. Ordinary sugar was 14 yuan and transit goods were 4.85 yuan. The local factory refined white sugar remained firm. Zhenji and Zhenyu had not offered any sugar for nearly 10 days. Yesterday, the market finally saw some continued sales. Zhenji and Zhenyu number 1 were both offered at 17.60 yuan, number 2 was 17.40 yuan, and number 3 was 17.20 yuan, an increase of about 1 yuan compared to the previous list price (24th). North-South Goods: Raw Peanuts' Sales Are Brisk

Yesterday, according to Qingdao telegraph, purchase prices for raw peanuts rebounded by 20 cents, and the tax exemption issue is expected to be implemented, making import and export easier to calculate. Sales improved, so market prices rebounded. In the morning, 2,000 bags of Tancheng peanuts were offered, with the higher grade at 6.55 yuan, and the second grade at 6.40 yuan, an increase of about 10 cents compared to the previous day. By the afternoon, the market became even tighter. 70 tons of Kaifeng peanuts were offered at 6.65 yuan, an improvement of about 60 cents compared to (1st). A small amount of Xuzhou peanuts were offered at 5.65 to 5.80 yuan, an increase of 20 cents compared to the previous day. Some sellers even wanted to sell at 6 yuan, and the trend was stable.

Tensions in Foreign Exchange, Silk Sales Grow Quieter

In recent days, foreign exchange has become tense, and silk sales in Europe and America have become increasingly sluggish. Yesterday morning, overseas telegraphs reported that silk prices were even lower. Chinese silk merchants did not have sufficient stock and held on to their goods, refusing to sell. Yesterday, only Dafeng and other firms imported 30 bales of white factory silk and 5 bales of white dried silk, with prices trending lower.

Reasons for the Price Drop in Antimony

丨Production Price Too Low and Disparity with Market Price丨

Antimony is a necessity for ordnance factories, mints, and printing houses. Recently, due to tight credit, buyers have been unable to absorb it, so there have been few purchases. The trade, with goods, is anxious to sell due to the large difference between production costs and local prices. The production cost is about 500 yuan per ton, whereas Shanghai currently stands at 845 yuan, a difference of over 345 yuan. Therefore, everyone is trying to sell, so the market standard fell by 40 to 50 yuan yesterday. It is estimated at 800 yuan, with only 200 tons traded. Moreover, the business of foreign firms is not moving. Future asking prices are feared to fall further.

Tinplate Shortage Appears Again

The 18-gauge tinplate has recently experienced a shortage again. The market situation is good, so the price has risen again by 50 cents, selling at 10.05 yuan per bundle. It is said that enamel factories and thermos manufacturers are in urgent need, so there are more buyers, and the asking price is improving, it is said.

Free Talk

Dissent on "Literature and Life"

— Wu Liping

A few days ago, in the "Free Talk" section, Mr. Lin Huanping wrote an article called "Literature and Life." He claimed that the motivation for writing this article was a letter he received from a poet who reported his intention to leave the literary world and delve into real life. The purpose was to indicate that the experience of actual life is the main condition for creating a literary figure. Based on this conclusion, he also expressed many opinions, using some well-worn phrases, and hyping up "life experience" and "image" to the skies. However, not a single word was said about what kind of life experience can practically capture images. Even if he says that observing life is possible and important, the possible conditions are still necessary. Mr. Lin did not tell us about this (assuming it is a) condition, nor did he state, "It cannot be covered in a short article." Thus, we have good reason to believe that Mr. Lin thought that once a literary figure ran into real life, all problems would be solved, as if real life guaranteed the creation of a great literary figure. Such a statement is optimistic enough; even more straightforward is "as a poet, I would very much agree with someone who wants to become a small clerk or junior staff member." This, of course, means going into real life in order to write poetry, emphasizing the six words "as a poet." Since Mr. Lin expressed his agreement with this attitude of participating in real life, he also expects great poems to be produced as a result. In fact, according to Mr. Lin's instructions and citations, he could easily guarantee that great poems will be produced in the future.

Although the article meanders quite a bit, it is actually just saying that literary figures must be able to, and must, be created through real life.

In principle, I completely agree with these two conclusions. What I disagree with is the explanation Mr. Lin added to these two conclusions.

First, I disagree that "as a poet," participating in real life can practically capture any images and can express the truth of life as its essence, because "as a poet" and a person are ultimately somewhat the same and somewhat different. Their attitudes towards participating in real life are also different, so their life content is also different. At this time, if what the poet captures and expresses belongs to the scope of a person, then its truthfulness becomes very questionable. If it belongs to one's own scope, then it is only one's own truth. So why bother delving into real life?

Second, I object to Mr. Lin citing Gorky as a witness to establish his argument, because Gorky did not participate in real life "as a poet" or "as a novelist," but only participated in real life as a person. This fact cannot be fabricated; his own life can testify to it. Although I cannot prove Balzac, Zola, Sinclair, and others in the same way, Mr. Lin has not proven that they participated in real life "as novelists."

I believe that if one wants to express the truth and essence of life, one must first live with the attitude of a person. Only direct life can touch the truth and essence of life. If one participates in real life with the qualification of a poet, even if one's attitude towards real life is not that of an onlooking game, it is at least using real life as a means. So, can one express the truth and essence of life? To give two very simple examples, Tao Yuanming returned to the countryside to farm, which should be considered participating in real life. However, he could only write poems such as "Leisurely Seeing the Southern Mountains." If "leisurely" is not the truth and essence of real life, then why is that? I think it must be because he participated in real life "as a poet." Closer to our time, the poet Chen Mengjia participated in the real life of the Shanghai Battle to find poetic material. Later, I heard that he published a book of poems dedicated to the Shanghai Battle, but unfortunately, it was not very great.

Therefore, participating in real life "as a poet" cannot fulfill Mr. Lin's wishes.

There are many others in China who are as optimistic as Mr. Lin. This phenomenon stems from the demands of reality. The poverty of Chinese literature is a fact, and the attempt to change this situation is a demand of reality. The answer to this demand is that literary figures are unanimously heading into real life. After they go, what happens? The answer is that everything is fine, according to Mr. Lin. But reality will disappoint Mr. Lin. If you don't believe it, ask the poets in the future if they want great poems, and you will know the result.

Literary figures are never created; they are just people who live in real life. Their works are just the experiences of direct life. They do not live in order to produce great works. If great literature appears in China, it will certainly not be the work of some "poet and novelist" type. However, there are no conditions for producing such literature now, but there is no need to imagine creating literary figures to decorate the lonely literary world.

A literary figure that cannot be created is equal to not being able to create a literary figure.

Night Market

— Lan Ru

The night market in Tokyo is even more lively than the daytime. If you want to buy cheap goods and books, you can go to the night market. Things that usually cost three or four dimes can be bought for only one dime at the night market. Because the entire economy is bankrupt and people have weak purchasing power, even though things are cheap to the point of a few cents, the piled-up goods remain as many every night. However, the people who stroll through the night market are like mountains and seas, always crowded to the point of being impenetrable. Naturally, seven or eight out of ten of these people are there to see the excitement or to take a walk to relieve boredom.

Because of the great famine in the Northeast, the male and female students standing on the street to collect donations are increasing day by day. They wear white sashes diagonally across their chests, with slogans such as "Northeast Relief Fund Raising Team" written on them. Some also write moving slogans, such as "Relief for Northeast Compatriots Who Are About to Die!" "Relief for Northeast Compatriots Suffering from Hunger and Cold!" Some use megaphones to shout loudly to passersby: "Northeast compatriots have eaten all the grass roots and tree bark, everyone donate some money to help!" But the passersby just walk past with their heads held high, no matter how the people holding donation boxes bow to them for help, they walk past without even glancing at them.

The radio is broadcasting melodious, intoxicating dance music. At this time, countless men and women are living sweet lives in movie theaters and dance halls. The Shinjuku night market is also different from three years ago. Putting aside the liveliness, what is astonishing at first sight is the male and female beggars with disheveled hair and skinny bones sitting under the terrazzo of Mitsukoshi. They wear ragged single clothes and shiver in the harsh north wind; in front of them is a piece of paper with words about how they were victimized and how poor they are. However, the eyes of the passersby are only cast on the brightly lit places, and their ears only hear the intoxicating music. Modern men and women hate these "馬鹿" (fools) who block the road.

×　　×　　×　　×

The night market is suitable for ordinary small citizens and poor students. Wealthy people go to large companies to buy things, so naturally they don't need to come to the night market to seek cheapness. Therefore, the night market invisibly symbolizes a certain part of human society.

I often talk to my friends about how the Japanese are indeed too amazing. No matter what they manufacture, it is small, exquisite, light, and beautiful, with a kind of magic that attracts you to buy it. For example, a small box for storing tacks or pen nibs, rouge and powder, can be bought for only three or five cents. So the ladies who like small gadgets spare no effort to take out all the money in their purses and send it to the night market. It is because the goods are too cheap that everyone's consumption is particularly high, just like the devaluation of the Japanese yen, the number of students studying in Japan is increasing day by day. On the surface, it seems that we are taking advantage of Japan by coming to study at this time, but in fact, when they are experiencing economic panic, large groups of Chinese students are coming to give them money. No wonder they desperately say: "Arigato, gozaimasu." (This sentence is a casual transliteration)

Unless you have particularly strong reason, I'm afraid no one can resist the temptation of material things. When you go to the night market, even a person who loves money like life will give away at least a few dimes to the Japanese. The only thing that can control your emotions and prevent you from buying those beautiful and cheap things is not reason, but money.

The night market in Kanda mostly sells books, while the night markets in Shinjuku and other places sell various daily necessities, clothing, and food.

Blood-red lights, soul-stirring music, noisy hawking, tragic cries for help... create the symphony of the Tokyo night market.

Face

— Jia Zhifang

Clever people often dress themselves up, like gentlemen or ladies. In short, besides a set of usual wide clothes, their characteristics are a pair of slightly furrowed eyebrows and a light nasal sound that indicates contempt, to teach the "ignorant and foolish" or "lowly people" in their eyes.

As soon as they come out, they point one finger to the sky and one finger to the ground, saying: "In the universe, I am the only one who is supreme." Others seem to be like mud statues sculpted in temples, looking at the bare-chested, prodigal-like Buddha, who should be "standing gods" or simply sleep under their big toes.

If they are "genuine literary figures" from the university's literature department, then they say to someone who doesn't have the ability to receive the same education as them, but who still dabbles in literature and writes something:

"Have you read Dante? Have you read a better outline of literature or something?"

This is said with a strong tone of pity; on the other hand, it is enough to highlight one's own abundance of talent and erudition. If the person being taught is really too much, then it seems like they are too hurt. They can immediately temporarily abandon their identity, redden their eyes, straighten their noses, and declare that they will verbally criticize and denounce him. Then, words like "ignorant," "shallow," or even "willingly degenerate," "being used by others," etc., are enough to pile up a tomb, making it impossible for you to breathe. Only then will they be satisfied.

However, they themselves would never write an article to compete. Perhaps, as Kagawa Toyohiko said, they intentionally emphasize a "flaw of beauty"? But as historically proven, they are actually "golden branches and jade leaves," and probably don't need to move a finger to already be "celebrities" or something similar.

Therefore, they don't need us to "forcibly and rudely" strip off their wide clothes and tear off their powdered faces. They themselves are the most faithful artists of their own art. That is, their faces have already been painted subtly and vividly by themselves. Although they have no works, it is said that they are also quite cultivated. They close their eyes and say that others are "ignorant" and "shallow," and they are second to none.

However, counterfeit goods will always one day reveal their true form. Without us bothering to strip off their decorations and puncture their masks, people will also see that the painted faces are fake.

The Sounds of Qingdao

— Huanming

Every day, I hide in the house. The house faces south. From noon to noon, morning and night, the sea breeze blows incessantly.

During the day, I am busy doing this and touching that, but often I can't do anything really important. After eight o'clock at night, the entire Qingdao is shrouded in an atmosphere like late autumn.

"Sugar buns, bean buns..."

This drawn-out sound echoes desolately under the window. This sentiment is similar to the sound of selling white sugar and heart porridge late at night in the alleyways of the South. The person selling bean buns is probably wearing black clothes. He carries a large basket on his arm, and in the other hand, he holds an oil lamp. He stops at the door, shouts twice, hesitates a few steps, and then slowly shuffles away.

At this time, there is probably always fog at sea. I open the window and look towards the sea. The red light on Little Qingdao flickers hazily. It's very beautiful, but also very lonely. When there is fog, the harbor also "whoo, whoo" emits a groan to warn passing ships. The sound waves are mixed with the roaring of the sea tide surging against the rocks. Sometimes, I can also hear the sound of shouting "Car!" carried by the sea breeze. At this time, the "Luo Han Qigong Treatment Center" across the street gradually becomes lively. The sound of whips cracking resounds strangely...

I once secretly went to "sightsee." It was like this: the person being treated took off his upper body and circulated his energy, letting the whip jump on his body. It is said that this can also cure diseases, and this kind of treatment is very believed and popular among a segment of the population in Qingdao. I also have illnesses, but I have not dared to treat them in this way.

I live in an alleyway house in Shanghai. The first sound in the morning is "pouring out the chamber pot." The sound of the clam shell scrubbing the chamber pot, "sha sha sha," is absolutely not heard in the North. What replaces the "sha sha sha" of the southern morning is the sound of the boiling water whistle, "li li li," from the boiling water shop. This boiling water shop is equivalent to the "tiger stove" in the South, but there are also differences: they don't use iron pots to boil water, but rather a large lead-skinned cylinder, and there is also a tap for tap water installed underneath. Selling boiling water is a subsidiary business of the general store. The general store has vegetables, fruits, and all kinds of daily household sundries. Not only do they sell "Aji-no-moto" (Japanese), but sometimes you can even buy monosodium glutamate! I have been in the South for many years and have never seen "Aji-no-moto" in a southern goods store. This should be a "difference between North and South," right? ... At first, I was very fortunate that tap water was, after all, not a foreign product, but now I know that the tap water used in my home is exported by the Japanese-capitalized match company. My father said:

"Sales are the best..."

When a person is lonely and bored, he often leans against the window and stares blankly at the road, or listens to the clattering of donkey carts on the road. The people pulling the carts must be "the blackest people in China," wearing black clothes and pants, with their lapels open, revealing their dark brown chests. Their faces are stained with coal ash. They advance three steps and retreat two steps on the sloping street, leaning at a 50- or 60-degree angle. The shoes they wear are also black - black "labor shoes." Of course, they are also Japanese goods.

On the street, the rhythmic sound of wooden clogs can be heard everywhere. Japanese housewives carry "large bundles" (this is for insiders), bending over and running to the "big vegetable market" to buy things. The shop assistants pile on smiling faces, warmly greeting them. Their tone and demeanor are just like "Japanese devils," without any sense of shame...

Even the most basic, most foolish shop assistants know a few words of Japanese to greet their customers.

Seashore

The American flagship floats quietly at anchor. "Pat, pat, pat," the small steamboat carries white sailors alongside the "pier."

"Richa..."

They jump into the car in a noisy group, pointing ahead: "U.S. Bar"

"Aye!" They rush towards Zhongshan Road like flying.

The sorrow of the Southerners, and the sorrow of the Chinese:

"Where is your hometown, sir..."

"I'm from Shandong. Are you, old brother, from, uh, Hebei? Or..."

"I'm from Zhejiang..."

"Oh," his face seems to have changed color a bit: "Zhejiang, Zhejiang, is probably in the South? Then, sir, are you a 'Southerner'?"

"Southerners" and "Northerners" are divided the most clearly here. They are divided as clearly as Northerners and Japanese.

The sounds of Qingdao are full of the sentiment of Dalian!

But there are also differences; because Dalian is even cooler than Qingdao! No, there is one more thing that is different. Geographically speaking, Dalian is further north than Qingdao.

Tomorrow (7)

— (By Joseph Conrad) Translated by Wu Xiangyu

"He must think he has 'planned ahead' for you to some extent. That's the best way for daughters... That's the husband..." He winks. Miss Bessan is engrossed in her knitting work, blushing slightly.

"Bessan! My hat!" Old Javir suddenly shouted madly. He had been sitting under the tree without saying a word. He didn't move, like a strange, absurd idol in superstition. He never spoke, but when looking for him, when speaking to her about her, he always shouted rudely. At that time, he never softened his embarrassing speech. Her way of dealing with it was to be completely silent; he would continue to shout until she came to serve him - that is, until she came to shake his arm, or put the mouthpiece of his pipe in his teeth. He was one of the few blind people who smoked. When he felt the hat had been placed on his head, he immediately stopped making noise. Then he stood up, and the two of them walked through the gate together.

He leaned heavily on her arm. In their slow, laborious steps, she seemed to be dragging a large, indecisive block of wood to confession. Usually, they immediately crossed the road (the two cottages were built in the fields near the sea entrance, two hundred yards from the end of the street). After a very, very long time, they were still in front of people, groping to walk up the wooden steps to the seawall. The seawall meandered from east to west, blocking the waters of the English Channel, like an abandoned railway embankment, on which no train had ever run. Groups of burly fishermen appeared from the horizon, walked along the coast for a while, and then slowly disappeared. Their brown nets, like the webs of huge spiders, were laid out on the uneven grass on the slope to dry. The people in the town, looking from the end of the street, could recognize from their slow little steps that it was Javir and his daughter, Captain Hagbolt, aimlessly... The surroundings of his two small houses also had to raise their heads to see where their walk had reached.

He still regularly published advertisements in the Sunday newspaper searching for Harry, Hagbolt, he first told Bessan, these newspapers could be read in all parts of the world. At the same time, he seemed to think that his son was still in England - very close to Colebrook, he could definitely find him "tomorrow." Bessan didn't use many words to oppose that opinion, only saying that if that was the case, the advertising fee was wasted; Captain Hagbolt should still calculate how he was making a living from that weekly shilling (worth two and a half shillings). She declared that she didn't know how he was relying on that to survive. Her tone must have made him doubt and have a short period of sadness in his heart. "People are doing this," he pointed out. The newspaper had a full page dedicated to advertisements searching for missing relatives. He even had to take the newspaper to show her. He and her wife had been advertising for several years; but she was an impatient woman. The news from Colebrook came just one day after his funeral; if she had not been so impatient, she might still be here waiting for a long time. "You are not an impatient woman, my dear."

"Sometimes I am with you, and I can't bear it," she always replied.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Women's Rights and French

— Pi

Chairman Fu Bingchang of the Legislative Yuan's Foreign Affairs Committee recently went to Hong Kong from Beijing, passing through Shanghai. Before leaving Shanghai, he spoke with a reporter on the train about Article 239 of the Criminal Code regarding adultery, which was quite interesting (the original text is omitted). I have two doubts about Fu's remarks: (1) a doubt about the issue of women's rights; (2) a doubt about French.

In the past two decades or so, the women's rights movement has been extremely high, as if women's rights were insignificant to some extent. After reviewing the second criminal law review case passed by the Legislative Yuan, there is a provision that "a married woman who commits adultery with another person shall be sentenced to imprisonment for a term not exceeding one year, and the adulterer shall be subject to the same punishment." The women's community believes that this is a provision that insults women, and they are greatly indignant. They joined women's circles inside and outside Beijing to petition in Beijing. As a result, the Legislative Yuan re-deliberated and changed it to "a person with a spouse, etc." Such a satisfactory result is rare in history, if we look at it historically, for men to go to Beijing to petition due to some problem and be able to obtain such a satisfactory result. Therefore, women's rights have not been seen to decline in any way, this is one thing.

Fu also said, "This case was originally passed to be removed from the criminal law, but later because some members of the Legislative Yuan wanted to stipulate a practice that has not changed for thousands of years in China (referring to punishing married women who commit adultery). Therefore, there was a second review of the criminal law passed. This time, because of the opposition of the women's community, when repeated discussions were held, some members were opposed by their wives, so those who previously advocated stipulating a thousand-year practice reversed their previous advocacy and instead demanded equal regulations." From this point of view, the "wife power" of the legislators is several times higher than that of the legislators. Why is there still a women's rights movement? This is another matter.

The so-called women's rights movement is because women's rights are less than men's rights, and husband's rights are higher than wife's rights, so there is a demand for equality between men and women. Now women's rights are higher than everything, and wife's rights are superior to husband's rights, which is completely contrary to the facts. Women's rights are higher than everything, originally from today onwards, the so-called "Hedong Lion's Roar," "Ji Chang's Fear of His Wife," etc., there are many romantic historical examples. I think someone will definitely initiate a men's rights movement in the future to resist the women's community, which may also be expected.

Also, the currently revised article states, "A person with a spouse who commits adultery with another person shall be sentenced to imprisonment for a term not exceeding one year, and the adulterer shall be subject to the same punishment." Since the article is stipulated in this way, adultery by a person without a spouse cannot be used as an example. Suppose a person with a spouse commits adultery with a person without a spouse, then the person without a spouse is presumably not guilty, and cannot be convicted for committing adultery with a person with a spouse. The article stipulates this clearly, but Fu Bingchang said, "Prostitutes are also guilty of the crime that article deserves." I am not only speaking out for the prostitute community, but also want to appeal for those without spouses who commit adultery with others, because how can prostitutes who entertain patrons know whether they have spouses? The same situation applies to those without spouses who commit adultery with others. Therefore, the phrase "the adulterer shall be subject to the same punishment" is somewhat inconsistent with the wording, because in the case of a person with a spouse committing adultery with a person without a spouse, is the adulterer guilty of the same crime or a different crime? This point is not clearly stipulated in French, which is a real doubt.

If it is said that the difficulties in which prostitutes will find themselves in the future are not necessarily visible. As long as the French law clearly stipulates that those without spouses are not included in this example, or the sentence "the adulterer shall be subject to the same punishment" is cancelled, then there will be a way for prostitutes to deal with it. Just paste a red paper slip on the door, "This apartment only entertains guests without wives. Guests with wives are not entertained. We hereby declare and ask for your forgiveness." In this way, they will not be innocently punished.

On "Deception"

— Li An

I feel that the Chinese people in the world are the most capable of deceiving people, and also the easiest to be deceived by others. Therefore, the art of "deceiving the world and stealing a name" is most popular in China; as long as a person has one point of ability, and can also have nine points of "deceiving the world and stealing a name" skills, he will definitely be a popular figure in society; on the contrary, even if you have nine points of true learning, but do not have one point of "deceiving the world and stealing a name" ability, you will never be allowed to stand out in your life. The fundamental crux of this problem is that the atmosphere of boasting and pretense is too prevalent from top to bottom. People are unwilling to be practical in everything, and only know how to show off and put effort into appearances. Therefore, in such a depressed year, clothing stores are still constantly opening; while the circulation of popular newspapers is still less than 200,000 copies. This indicates that knowledge is only stored in the heart, while clothing is a good thing that can deceive the world.

Let me give a few examples! A Western charlatan runs to China, hangs up the title of professor, and stays at the Waldorf Hotel, and someone will voluntarily give him money. On the contrary, Wang Tiezui of the City God Temple, although he also knows how to flaunt "King Wen" and "Duke Zhou," is far behind professors in business acumen. Wang Tiezui has never put effort into the word "deception," and is not as insightful as professors about the Chinese people's tendency to be deceived. Therefore, Tiezui suffers a loss. A few months ago, there was a problem with literary heritage in the literary world. Everyone was pulling in Gorky, Chekhov, etc., as window dressing in a lively manner. In my opinion, China's literary heritage seems to be figures like Qu Yuan, Zhuangzi, and Confucius. However, if you have the courage to bring up people like Qu Yuan, no one will look at you. Gorky and Chekhov are fashionable, and the general public will show respect to you. This consciousness is the same as when you go to a store to buy things. American goods are certainly better than Chinese goods, and MadienChina seems to be more superior than Made in China. Therefore, domestic tobacco companies have all stopped printing Chinese on their products!

Because I am dissatisfied with modern "American-style education," I have repeatedly proposed adopting the "Shuyuan system" to improve modern education. I have spent some effort studying it and feel that this system is the most reasonable and natural education; it is comparable to Oxford-style education, and adopting this system is the best way to save modern education. However, the Shuyuan education system was unfortunately produced in China, and China simply does not have a good system. I wrote an article about the Shuyuan system and took it to a friend for discussion. He said to me, "If you want this article to attract people's attention, the first thing you should do is change 'Shuyuan system' to 'Oxford system.' The Chinese people are good at deceiving people and good at being deceived by others, so you must deceive them a little." He smiled as he said this, and I smiled too.

I remember someone once said: "The difficulty in China lies in the excessive atmosphere of boasting and pretense from top to bottom." Boasting and pretense means not being practical, and also deceiving the world and stealing a name. Today we advocate something, and tomorrow we advocate another thing. Making declarations and sending telegrams, of course, there is a grand and eloquent embellished article, but ask how many things these advocates can do themselves?

People who rely on the word "deception" to parasitize in society are everywhere, like gilded chamber pots placed in society to do the work of deception. They flaunt the titles of PhDs, returned students, educators, and scholars, and swagger through the world doing ghostly tricks. If these masks are not exposed, there is no remedy.

Page 18

After the Plan Was Realized

— Hong Ben

To put it in a twisted way, the realization of my plan owes a considerable debt to that nameless petty thief. If my leather coat hadn't been stolen by him, this plan definitely wouldn't have been realized this year. Because I have always been a person who loves to talk but doesn't like to act, many things, I think about so thoroughly in my heart and say so beautifully with my mouth, but I have never seen them put into practice. This is my old habit, and I truly feel more than a little ashamed when I say it.

Last year, at a certain banquet, because I was wearing an inappropriate long gown, I was ridiculed by others. On the spot, I pondered in my mind and silently vowed to make a suit. But, alas, "time passed and the heart calmed," and by the next day I had forgotten about it again. Firstly, it was indeed because the "large amount" at the time was not enough for me to spend. But in reality, it was mostly due to "being too lazy to put it into practice." I would rather stop attending banquets afterwards when I suddenly remembered that I had no suit to wear, fearing that I would be ridiculed by others again.

It was only when I encountered the "iron-faced and ruthless" petty thief, who stole my leather coat in just five minutes of negligence, that I moved from "thinking" and "talking" to drafting a plan, and recently, I actually put on a suit.

Although I have already put it on, there is still a story to tell, which is the state of mind when trying it on. Having always been such a rustic person, now wearing a straight suit, I felt strangely flustered. Pacing back and forth in the room, I struggled with the first step, lacking the courage to step out of the door. In fact, when I walked out, everyone looked at me with nothing more than an indifferent glance.

However, my mood was still somewhat uneasy: I always vaguely saw people staring at me, discussing me, even satirizing me, saying that someone like me should never wear such a straight suit. Although I have been wearing the suit for a month, this scene still lingers around me, swirling before my eyes, making me extremely uneasy.

Secondly, it has added a kind of burden. I have always been a casual person. In the past, I not only didn't care about my clothes but also didn't cherish them. I would casually wipe the table with my sleeves, use my lapel to hold things, and sleep in my clothes at night, all of which were very common. But now I can't do that anymore. In order to maintain the beauty of the suit, I have to keep my back straight when walking, wipe the dust off the stool before sitting down, and be careful not to drip oil stains on my clothes when eating. What makes me most painful is that before taking off my clothes to go to bed, I have to fold the creases of my pants very carefully before I can sleep peacefully. Otherwise, if I throw them around like my old Chinese-style trousers, and the creases disappear when I put them on in the morning, wouldn't that be a laughingstock for suit wearers?

As for the trouble of wearing it, such as tying the tie again and again, polishing the leather shoes again and again, brushing the clothes again and again, and looking in the mirror again and again, these are minor matters and need not be mentioned further.

Recently, it has even stirred up a rumor. Several colleagues who I often interact with have unanimously said that I have changed too suddenly and must have some kind of ambition or bad intentions. Heaven knows! What's most annoying is that a few days ago, when I saw a friend I hadn't seen for a long time, he blurted out, "I heard you're in love now, and wearing a suit is solid proof." A friend's letter even affirmed that I had made progress in my career. It's truly being wronged alive.

At this point, I feel that I can't wear a suit, at least not someone like me.

The Story of Socks

— Wen Hei

Because I had nothing to do, I went for a stroll on the road after dinner.

The night in the city is a city that never sleeps. The electric lights are so bright that the road is almost like daytime. Also, neon lights draw patterns in the air and write large characters, red, green, purple, blue, colorful, dazzling people's eyes. As I walked, I came to the entrance of a general store, where many people like me were standing on the road, listening to the radio broadcast on the door. A passage in the Suzhou dialect was telling a story. I didn't understand it and wanted to leave, but a glance at the glass display window, some cheap daily necessities attracted me. A two-pound thermos only costs forty cents, enough. I remembered that I used to buy a thermos for one dollar each, regretting not waiting a little longer to buy it now. There was already a thermos on the table at home, it could not tempt my heart to save money. However, it was also because of the cheap thermos that I wanted to know if there were any more bargains to be bought. Oh, socks are one dollar for five pairs. Thinking that I only have one pair of socks at home, and there's a hole in the front and a hole in the heel, I'll buy them for one dollar. Besides being enough for myself, I can also give my younger brother two pairs. Having made up my mind, I walked into its door. Considering myself as a customer, I found it funny to myself, what's so impressive about a one-dollar customer? In this way, I became humble and felt embarrassed for a long time, not daring to open my mouth, but the shop assistants paid close attention to me. A gentleman in a long robe ran over to greet me, "Hat?" He thought I was going to buy a hat. Or maybe he thought his shop's hats were the best. I scratched my head to indicate that I didn't want to buy a hat, but at the same time, I glanced at the side where many hats were piled up, subconsciously wanting to see what his hats looked like. After glancing at them, I immediately felt that I should reply to the shop assistant, so I said "Socks", considering it as correcting his mistake and indicating my purpose in entering his shop. In this way, he became busy, and I felt more important, considering myself not a person who just came to wander around but a customer.

It was already winter, and the cold wind was still howling in the streets, so it was no wonder that he took out woolen socks for me to see. I said it wasn't this kind. But I couldn't say "cheap" for a long time. He misunderstood me, thinking that the color was wrong. The original color was dark red, so he took out a light yellow one. When he was closing the box to get another one, I already felt sorry for him: If I still didn't want it when he opened another box, wouldn't that be too impatient and unhappy for him? I got anxious and didn't care about much, directly telling him, "One dollar for five pairs." He didn't get angry but smiled at me and said, "Oh, yes, yes." In this way, when he took out the socks that were one dollar for five pairs for me to choose, I felt that I had to buy them, otherwise I would be too sorry. Moreover, at the same time, I felt that cheap goods were so-so, and it wouldn't be right to be too picky. The deal was done, I took out one dollar, and he wrapped up the five pairs of socks for me.

Leaving the store, I still heard his polite words, "Come again next time." I didn't reply to him anything, but it attracted the attention of the people standing at the door listening to the radio broadcast, who looked at me with envious and curious eyes.

Returning home, I put down the socks and did other things. But when I put the socks on my feet the next morning, I pulled them hard, and they broke! I broke two pairs in a row. Fortunately, the third pair didn't break. But I had already learned the lesson of being greedy for cheap things.

Night in the Artery

— You Qi

Time is moving, the city is moving, people are moving.

After the curtain of night is drawn, the pulse of the metropolis is in turmoil, with big mouths open everywhere, swallowing people wildly. Along this wind-swept breath, the crowd of people rolls on.

"Darling," she smiles, this word is called out so sweetly.

"Hmm," putting down the evening paper in his hand, he rushes over. The blood, as if unable to contain this heart, makes it jump involuntarily.

Soft velvet sofa, a bronze table lamp on the glass panel, a cotton gauze lampshade embroidered with flowers, and the light from the lampshade of ocher color bathes their faces, what a happy couple!

"I want..." Again, she giggles, playing with the narrow cuffs, "to go to Shanghai, okay?"

The road is in turmoil, people's feet are in turmoil, the sound is in turmoil...

×　　×　　×

"Hey, Lao Zhang, Lao Li, let's have a midnight snack!"

Really, mentioning midnight snack, can make Lao Zhang's heart move, he thought, this should be the right time, the sky is high and the air is crisp, the crabs are fat and the chrysanthemums are yellow, it is time to open up and drink heartily.

Fat crabs, really enough to make one drool, at the intersection of Ri Sheng Lou, in that gray-blue big tank, one by one, look, how big, Yangcheng Lake's.

Surrounding the small charcoal fire, surrounding the small round table, pinching the small cups!

"Drink, drink as much as you can!" Then, he gulps down wine, his face flushed, his heart as hot as charcoal fire.

In the Dancing hall:

When the pulse of the metropolis is slightly still, he walks out of the stone steps of the office with a tired mood. Somehow, when the dazzling light touches him, the fatigue will run away.

Music, lingeringly sounding, all around, it's all dark, on the roof, this time it's green, gloomy, like falling asleep.

Dance, what is sprinkled on this top is the warp of the sky,

, this lingering weft is exactly the wandering soul!

The fragrance of clothes, the fragrance of powder, those pairs, are the fragrance of love.

However, in the pulse of the night, there may also jump out a few big men from the oblique waist!

Stop, don't sound, leave the money. You may also be caught by the clothes without being vigilant!

Thank you, okay, count it as eight cents.

Night, continues in this moving pulse.

Opening "Shuangwen Worships the Moon"

Waiting for the moon in the West Chamber, the moon gradually rises. Hongniang follows and serves the beautiful lady. The young lady is like a jade hairpin, without flaws. Two gold hairpins divide her cloud-like hair. Double pearl earrings flutter. White silk shirt exudes a different fragrance in the wind. Jade arms wear a pair of gold bracelets. A pearl hanging on her chest dazzles the eyes. Embroidered handkerchief in her pointed hand. Pink trousers tied around her slender waist. Gauze knee pads and silk ribbons. Red embroidered shoes with perfect toe. Standing by the Wild Goose Cloud Pavilion. Nine lotus lanterns hung in front of the pavilion. Dew wets the green moss, and the white rabbit stares. The wind blows butterflies dreaming in the shade of flowers. Red pear trees are full of red pear blossoms. Peony flowers wither in the peony pavilion. Leaning on the Cloud Terrace, too lazy to pluck the lute. Banana leaf fans swat fireflies. I am ten thousand miles away and see Zhang Junrui. Zhang Sheng meets his soulmate in the Buddhist temple. Retreating the bandit soldiers shows the meritorious Qilin Pavilion. Good is Kongming in the Romance of the Three Kingdoms. Tonight, the bright moon shines in the Emerald Garden. Kneeling on the brocade futon, secretly confessing sincerity. I wish to dismantle the toad palace, hang up the gold list. A happy marriage, a wedding candle tied with flowers. Eternal reunion, a hundred-year marriage.

National Studies

Ms. Jiang Bingmei Tang Poetry

Huaxing (1260) 9 AM to 10 AM

Drinking Alone by Moonlight Li Bai

Do you not see the Yellow River's waters descend from heaven, rushing into the sea, never to return? Do you not see the high hall, bright mirror, grieving over white hair, like green silk in the morning, turning into clouds at dusk? When life is fulfilling, enjoy it to the fullest, let not the golden cup face the moon in vain! Heaven has endowed me with talent, which must be useful, even if a thousand gold is spent, it will return. Cook sheep and slaughter cattle, let's have fun, we must drink three hundred cups at once. Cenfuzi, Danqiusheng, drink up, don't stop your cup! I will sing a song for you, please all of you listen carefully. Bell drums and jade delicacies are not worth cherishing, but I wish to be drunk forever and not wake up. In ancient times, sages and virtuous men were all lonely, only drinkers left their names. Chen Wang held a banquet at Ping Le Palace in the past, ten thousand coins for a dou of wine, indulging in joy. Why does the host say he has little money? You must get drunk before me. Five-flower horse, thousand-gold fur coat, call the boy to take them out to exchange for fine wine, to dispel ten thousand years of sorrow with you.

Shanghai Shenbao Local Supplement Film Special Issue

Hollywood's Golden Child

— A trickle

=A child's value is 150 times that of gold=

=The cost of childbirth cannot be calculated with common sense=

Some say that the value of a child born to a Hollywood movie star is equal to the value of their weight in gold. But if we calculate more meticulously, we can know that a child born to a female star is actually one hundred and fifty times more valuable than its weight in gold. Do you say this is baseless? Well, for example, if a child is born weighing ten pounds, according to the value of gold of the same weight, it is only worth $58,000. But its real value is no less than one million U.S. dollars. Isn't this more than one hundred and fifty times more valuable than its weight in gold? Let's take Joan Blondell's child as an example. When calculating the price of a child, we are not limited to the cost of childbirth and upbringing; we must also add the money that has to be spent because of the child, or the money that could be saved and earned more if there were no child. In this way, Joan's salary loss due to having a child has already reached 35,000 yuan. The film company's contract can generally be extended according to the length of the maternity period. Therefore, if a female star takes a year off work due to childbirth, her contract will also be extended for one year until the original contract term expires. The salary loss during this period can be calculated on paper, but the actual loss she suffers is more than this number and cannot be statistically calculated. You must know that the audience's preferences for movies are very changeable. If a young female star's physical condition is affected by childbirth, the loss will be enormous. If she stays away from the screen for too long, the audience forgets her name, or new female stars take her place, then her loss is unimaginable, or even irreparable for life.

Someone calculated that the time a female star in Hollywood stops working due to childbirth is generally eight months: three months before childbirth and five months after childbirth. But many female stars spend a year or a year and a half giving birth to a child. According to Helen Twelvetrees' calculation, she lost no less than $100,000 in a very short period of time to have a son. Joan Crawford took three years off to have a son, and now she finds it very difficult to return to the screen. Clara Bow had to reject many lucrative contracts because she wanted to have a child.

Furthermore, the cost of childbirth is generally thought to be borne by the female star herself. In fact, the film company's losses are also enormous. When Joan Blondell was filming her last film before giving birth, the special equipment prepared for her in the company was considerable. Moreover, the working hours were shortened every day, and many supporting actors and staff had to act according to her schedule. Therefore, Joan Blondell's various losses in the company when she gave birth to a child already amounted to hundreds of thousands of yuan. It is said that Hollywood film companies spend $300 per minute when filming. If it is filming a large scene, the loss is even more than this. When Joan was filming (Sames), it is impossible to calculate how many minutes were spent, but it is not absolutely unreasonable to say that tens of thousands of dollars were spent.

Two male stars, Bing Crosby and Harold Lloyd, spent a lot of special money on their children. That is certainly an exception, but it also shows how much money movie stars can spend. Harold Lloyd said that he only knew the benefit of having money when his child was born. If he didn't have money, his child would not have survived. It turned out that his child was a premature birth and had to be placed in a glass incubator, wrapped in cotton, and slowly taught to breathe and eat things. That was the most expensive equipment in science, and only the richest people could afford it. Bing Crosby's twin sons were also premature. When they were born, each weighed only four pounds, but they are still alive today using the same method. As for the hospital fees during childbirth, the stars pay ten times more than ordinary people. They hire special nurses, who take turns in three shifts a day. In addition, there are many places where medical experts need to be consulted, and the cost is even more shocking to say.

In addition, an even larger expense is the security fee. We have heard a lot about Hollywood kidnappers and how stars protect their children. Marlene Dietrich specially sent her daughter to Europe for her safety. The rest of the stars hire bodyguards or add defensive equipment, which can be said to be painstaking. But we won't talk about that here.

Movie Review

Review of "Judge Priest"

— Stone Axe

"Judge Priest" showing in Shanghai

The word "humor" has become popular in China. We all know George Bernard Shaw in England, but there is also a great humorist in Hollywood, America, who earns top salaries and is famous in the film industry, Will Rogers, who has not yet been recognized by our Chinese people. This master of humor absolutely adheres to the American creed of peace first. He often resolves disputes with subtle words, and his life truths can turn hostility into friendship. In the films he has starred in in the past, we can understand that he is such a wonderful person. It seems to be a higher level than George Bernard Shaw's deliberately portraying and wasting vitality satire.

This "Judge Priest" we must know that it is adapted from a novel extracting some personality traits about Judge Priest. We can regard it as an anecdote. We can see that this judge is extremely emotional and sympathetic to the public. His personality is almost contradictory to law and politics. Therefore, we have a good show to watch here. He is trying cases with the principle of "making the people not compete by weighing measures and leveling scales," and he is also working as a matchmaker for people, so that those who are in love can become husband and wife. On the surface, he is humorous and cynical, but in reality, he is a person who laughs with tears in his eyes.

The American Civil War is indeed a glorious war history that can be praised. The heroes who captured flags and killed generals at that time were fighting for freedom, which is indeed more valuable than any world war. It is very gratifying to use this war to secretly set off the theme of the whole play. In order to prevent the performance of such stories from being warlike, many permanently enthusiastic Southern Melodies such as My Kentucky Home, Old Folks at Home, Dixie, Marching Through Georgia have been added to increase the audience's pleasure, especially these types of songs must be sung by black people.

The interspersed humor is very suitable for humorous conditions, and it is completely different from ordinary slapstick comedies. Eating ice cream and having a sugar party is very novel. The supporting actors are also veterans, so they complement each other.

This is a film worth introducing.

Did you know?

— Donglin

LeRoy, the most beloved child star in Hollywood, who first appeared on the screen in "When the Night is Deep" and gained fame, is now just one year old, but he has already saved enough tuition to graduate from university.

According to Adolphe Menjou, the first master of dressing in Hollywood, if you want to be a gentleman, you should wear the Chester coat, Gary Cooper's coat, Lowell Sherman's hat, Robert Montgomery's tie, William Powell's pants, and Clark Gable's shoes.

The most popular star in America right now. You won't believe it, but it's Shirley Temple, who is only four years old this year! Of course, she will never read the lines in the film; but she can memorize the lines faster than ordinary actors. Her method is: first, her mother reads the lines to her carefully twice, and then she says it herself in the same way, so she has already memorized it.

Mae West has a total of fifteen different kinds of ordinary clothes. She changes one of them every day. She has her nails manicured three times a week, of course, all painted pink. There is not even a piece of pajamas in her home, all of them are those luxurious evening dresses!

George Bancroft used to be from a circus troupe, so the "Happy Go Lucky" that was recently shown in Shanghai is his autobiography.

Carole Lombard was a famous high jumper in her school days.

John Bowers held a wedding ceremony in his new film "The Life of the West": this can be said to be his "first" wedding on the screen.

Douglas Montgomery's teeth are the whitest in Hollywood.

"Escape" Becomes Real

— Qingyun

Since "Escape" returned from filming on location in Zhangjiakou, last night it resumed filming the scene of the Northeastern people fleeing during the "September 18th" Incident. Director Yue Feng and Tang Na specially made hundreds of fake bombs with the same shape as real bombs but containing a small amount of gunpowder in advance in order to make the war scenes realistic. Although these bombs are not real bombs, they can explode if thrown hard on the ground and can also cause damage. When filming this interior scene of the "September 18th" Northeastern Incident last night, Wang Yin, Yuan Meiyun, Cang Yinqiu, Ye Juanjuan, Qin Tong, Jin Xingan, etc., played the Northeastern people. Dozens of other male actors played soldiers of a certain country, throwing bombs at the Northeastern refugees. For a time, the sound of bombing and the cries of refugees were mixed together, and the scene was realistic. The neighbors on all sides of the company heard the sound and suspected that the war had restarted, and they were too panicked to sleep. Unexpectedly, at this tense moment, several bombs were thrown at the faces of Ye Juanjuan, Qin Tong, and Jin Xingan. When they heard a loud bang, the faces of all three were injured by the explosion, and they fell to the ground in extreme pain. They were immediately helped up and rushed to a nearby hospital for treatment. Because the injuries were not very serious, they were discharged from the hospital after the doctor applied medicine and bandages. (sic)

Speaking of "Bigamy"

— Fire

"Bigamy" is not only a success of the director's skills, not only the beautiful light of the photography, but also the superior contribution of each actor's expression. It is undoubtedly a super special work in the Chinese film industry.

Lao Gao and Xiao Gao are a happy couple here. Xiao Gao plays a feudal woman in an old-fashioned family, and Lao Gao is the opposite of her. He is a modern college student who likes romance. Under this conflict of new and old ideas, all kinds of tragedies are caused. Lao Gao was imprisoned for bigamy and abandonment. The compensation for the loss and the burden of alimony bankrupted the entire family. We can see many soulless bodies wriggling and many painful shadows crawling. The director is Wu Cun, the director of "Wind," who once caused a sensation in the Chinese film industry. Under the destruction of four pairs of scissors, we cannot fully reveal it. This time in "Bigamy," we can see the director's "true face of Mount Lu." (sic)

Each submission must be stamped with a seal, otherwise it will not be paid for.

If the submission is a translation, please attach the original. English mixed in may be omitted.

Small Movie Talk

Mother-Daughter Relationship (Lady by Choice) (2)

— Zhongjia

The judge listened to the singing man's statement of his case, suppressing his laughter. In his heart, he wished he was there to see Pansy drunk and angrily beat the singer. But he dared not let Pansy know his joy, she had already been too presumptuous. So he sternly said to Pansy, "Why did you hit him?" Pansy put her hands on her waist and shouted with wide eyes, "Why? He was singing a mother's song!" Suddenly, there was a burst of laughter in the back of the courtroom, and the sound of small hands clapping. Judge Daley looked up and looked over to the place where the clapping was coming from, and he couldn't help but clench his lips. What he saw was a young woman wearing a loose fur coat and holding a large ostrich feather fan in one hand. How could he not recognize her? All the city's tabloids had published her photos, everyone had heard her name, and everyone had read her news. She was Ala Baneley, the feather fan dancer who caused a sensation in New York. Next to her was her stage manager, Kendall, and a policeman. Her publicist, Froote, followed behind. When Judge Daley was looking at Ala Baneley, Ala Baneley was still laughing at Pansy. Perhaps Ala Baneley heard Pansy's aversion to mother's songs and expressed sympathy to her. Or perhaps she felt that Pansy was a sketch of her old age. She felt that Pansy must have been as straightforward, quick-tempered, and intolerant of hypocrisy as she was when she was young. She also saw that Pansy must have been as beautiful and charming as she was when she was young, because her eyes, although old, still had a green afterglow. Her loose, disheveled hair must have been as golden as pure gold at first. Her mouth, although the corners had been pulled down by the years and wind and frost, must have been very moving in the past. She thought and couldn't help but feel scared. If she got old, she would definitely become like Pansy, unless Heaven had some special magic to stop that change. In the future, men would gradually restrain their smiles when they saw her. Or what she is drinking to refresh herself now will become her daily food in the future. Or she would be hungry and cold and wander around. Ala Baneley looked at Pansy as if she were looking at a mirror, reflecting her future vividly, and couldn't help but shudder. But while she was daydreaming, Pansy was also smiling at her. So she couldn't help but clap her hands and laugh again. Judge Daley was furious when he heard this, banged the gavel on the table, and shouted, "Silence!" His eyes glared fiercely at Ala Baneley, and then he asked Pansy again, "Why can't he sing mother's songs?" When the judge asked Pansy, she couldn't help but become furious again. All she heard was her shouting, "This shameless thing, his mother often beat her when she was alive. A year ago, he abandoned his wife and three children. So when he sang the line "Mother's warm and kind light shines from her eyes," I couldn't help but jump up and want to stab him. Judge, you would too, wouldn't you?" The judge pondered in his heart that it was no wonder Pansy. Strange Pansy... Poor Pansy, she has a loyal heart, but she is inevitably accused by others. Or his previous pity for her and releasing her was a misuse of leniency, which harmed her instead. This old woman really can't take care of herself. It would be best to find a safe place for her where she can have food to eat every day, a bath to wash every day, and a pillow to rest her head on and a blanket to cover her body every night. So he sternly rebuked, "Do you know how many times you've been here in a year?" Pansy did not answer. The judge calculated for her, "Seven times, isn't it? The last time I released you, you promised me that you wouldn't drink a drop of alcohol again. You've said many times that you wouldn't drink alcohol again. Now you're causing trouble again because of drinking!" (To be continued)
